O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	 O you, very dear son, I have completed this book which is the final part of the science of medicine along with its completion, and I have made the end through its explanations and by its clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	 And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	 And because the work of hands is foreign to our region and strange in every way, so the science has perished and decayed, and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in books of the ancients which the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	 And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed off and knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 And it seems to me that I want to revive the ordinance of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of cautery irons, and other tools of the work, with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	 And for this reason that no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	 And it is necessary for one who engages in this to be well-versed in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and flesh and the number of them, and the movement and rest of the moving and stationary veins, and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	 And for this reason said Hippocrates that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little; and likewise in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned should take care not to fall into error and harm people; just as I have often seen many of those who engage in this science and thus abandon their science and good judgment.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 For I saw a foolish doctor who cut an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 And I saw another doctor who removed a stone from a man with water, and the stone was large; he also took away a part of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	 And I had already been called to remove it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if one removed it he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 And I saw another physician who took care of the Duke of our land whose leg was broken, and with the break he had a wound; and the physician, full of ignorance, pressed the break onto the wound to splints with great force, and left no salve at all on the wound, and left it thus for a term; and commanded that it should not be unbound; and so it remained until the leg was entirely swollen and the foot came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 I was called to come to him, and hurried to come unbind the leg; and when I had unbound it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 But still, the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and it could not heal; and the corruption did not cease spreading through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	 And thus another doctor who opened an abscess, and then inflamed it through the malice of his arrogance.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	 For a chancre, when it is purged of black bile, one must not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that all the corruption can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 And therefore, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: that is to say, works where there is danger in many situations; and I will show in each place in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 For which reason it is necessary that you guard yourself, so that the foolish physician cannot speak ill of you. If you take up your arms in caution, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method, then by the grace of God you will come to safety and be praised; and leave behind dreadful diseases of serious illness; and remove your arms from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can go from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on a serious illness, lest you be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 I have composed this treatise according to III chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 The first chapter is about fire cautery and medicine-based cautery, and the chapter is organized from the head to the feet; and about the shapes of instruments, and the iron tools for cautery, and everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 The second chapter is about cutting and drilling, and cupping and wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things; and the chapter is organized with the shapes of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 The third chapter is about resetting dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is organized from the head to the feet, and with the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	 Just as we remember the work, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of help and harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 I say that the qualities of the aid, and of the harm, are the longest words and the subtlest science and the secret responses; and many of the wise have spoken about this, and they agreed on this; and few of their words satisfy me, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 I say that cautery helps universally in every complexion where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 In hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have discussed and said that cautery is great help there; and others said the opposite: that cautery is of no use for an illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 Car the nature of fire is so hot, and it should not be treated with heat for hot diseases, nor with drought; and he who says otherwise declares that cauterization greatly aids in hot and dry diseases that come into the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	 When you compare the body of man and his moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	 And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	 For I have found it sometimes through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 And nevertheless, let no one interfere with it except for he who has proven it, and who knows through long practice the chapter of cauterization, and the diversity of human complexions, and their predispositions and causes of their diseases, and their occurrences and the passage of time; we have no fear of other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	 Et toutes les médecins se sont réunies et ont convenu du cautère.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	 And know, son, that the cautery of fire together is one of the secrets of healing, and more beneficial than the cautery of burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	 Because fire is simple, and does not go beyond the member that it burns, nor harms any other member if possible.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 Burning medicines go from one member to another, spreading, and bring diseases of difficult healing to the members; and perhaps kill the patient. Fire, due to its power and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	 And this I have found through experiment and the length of my service and study that I have put into the art, and it was on the truth of things; and therefore I excuse myself for the length of speech, because it does not please me that I take away from you the secret that is in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives out diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	 And know, son, that they agreed on what time the cauteries should be done, and chose patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 And I say that a cautery is suitable in all seasons, because the harm that arises is put down by the help of the cautery; and also if the cautery is necessary for pain, it must be done swiftly and promptly, so that it does not await the time when greater evil comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 And never think of it thus, dear son, as the foolish physicians do; for the disease that is healed by cautery does not return; and they say so; but it is not as they believe, because a cautery is nothing but medicine which changes the complexion, dries the humors that are the cause of pain, and is more effective than medicine due to the swiftness of its power, and the virtue of its work and mastery.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	 And it is possible that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the disease and its virtue; and the superfluities are gathered in him by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in a place where there is little superfluousness and moisture, such as dental cauteries for pain, and similar things; and such pain does not return.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauteries are worthwhile after medication, but their thoughts are false. And cauteries are the last resort of medicine because when we administer certain treatments in some diseases and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	 Then it is clear that cauterization is the last resort in medicine, not at all according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 The ancients said that cauterization with a golden instrument is more beneficial than with iron, and those outside [the profession] said this only because of the quality of gold and the fineness of its substance; but they said that the place of cautery does not cause putrefaction, which is not true, for I have tested it and found that it is true in some men; and cauterization with gold is more beneficial than with iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 Nevertheless, when you heat a golden instrument, you cannot tell by the color of gold when it is hot enough, and it cools down quickly; and if you heat it too much, it melts in the fire; and so there are many obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	 And because of this, we use the fire cautery that we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	 Or I have ordered this chapter from head to toe, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	 of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	 This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the brain, and it has two advantages: one is due to a disease called "soda", and the other is due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and also due to excessive dreaming and toothache and throat pain, and also for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 The shape of this cautery is such that the patient should be purified by a dissolving medicine, modifying the head III or IV times, according to what the virtues and habits of the patient can tolerate; and then make the head of the patient's hair grow back.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 And then have the patient sit cross-legged between your hands, and place their hands on your feet; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and where your fingers will come, let it bleed from there. Then heat the cautery called "olivare", which has this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place it on the designated spot, and while descending and tightening your hand little by little in rotation; then lift your hand suddenly, and check the spot if you see a small bone I; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after that, take a piece of linen and place soft cotton inside, and put it on the spot, and leave it for III days; then put on a cloth soaked in butter; and leave it on until the burn is healed; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	 And said the ancients that the longer an open wound remains, the more it purges itself; and therefore, it helps to move (the limb).
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	 And some of them said that one should allow the cautery to continue until part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone, and it should be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 And others said that one should allow the cautery to continue and push so hard that a piece of bone as wide as a spindle, which women use for spinning, comes out, so that the humors may be moved out; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; afterwards, it must be cured and healed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me at all, except in some men where there is fear; and I think that I should leave them; for the head (of the bone) is weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we have shown in other members; and likewise when the patient's head is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more healing and useful to me, and with this one I work together for safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	 of an ancient pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 When there is chronic pain throughout the head that lasts for a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie", as well as purgatives for the head, oils, and poultices; and if cautery, as we have said before, does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Take care if the patient's head is of a strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize it slightly under that cautery which we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 After that, cauterize each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place called "vasselz"; and this is the place where cupping glasses are placed; and clean your hand so that you do not see it until the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and the cauteries for the horns should be finer than those used to cauterize the middle part of the head, and this is the method.
dou cautere dou chief	 From the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 When pain suddenly strikes in one part of the head and the illness extends to the eye, and the head is purged with cleansing medicines, and other treatments have been done as I said in the classification of diseases, and none of this helps: then you make cauteries in two ways, namely with water-based medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 The cautery with water-based medicine is done by taking a clove of garlic and removing its skin and putting it into the eye for two times, then make an incision on the temple where the pain is such that you can place the clove of garlic under the skin; and when it has been placed, bind it well and let it stay this way for twelve hours; and then unbind and pull off the bandage with the clove of garlic, and leave the wound like this for two or three days; then apply a plaster soaked in butter until it can heal.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 Après le cure d'onguent tant qu'il soit sané;
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 The iron cautery is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Heat the cautery which has this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a closed fist with a hollow in which there is a little cavity; and in the middle there is a small hole; and you place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand steady and twist the fire slightly until half the thickness of the cure is burnt; and lift your hand so that the outer part does not burn, which is outside, and an abundance of blood flows out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 After, place cotton in vinegar water, and put it on the place for III days; then put wet cotton in butter, and then cure the place from oiling until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery that is called "cultellare," do so at the point, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not very old.
de emigraine	 of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 When you cure migraine as we have said before in the division of illnesses, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery previously mentioned of medicine and iron does not help, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and immediately place it on the aching spot about half an inch long, and remove your hand once, and hold so that you do not cut the artery and that you do not reach the bone; and beware of the jawbone which moves when one eats, and let the nerve have no regard for movement or spasm in the patient, and beware of excessive bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or cutting has great fear and especially to those who are not knowledgeable and experienced; and leave the work half done; but I will tell you how one staunches blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you in the proper place in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And if you see that this cautery does not alleviate the disease, and the patient is tolerant, cauterize him on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on artery extraction, with a cautery that has two knives; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	 of the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	 When ear pain comes from cold, and one has used dissolving medicines and other cures that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery which is called "poin," of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After piercing all around the ear of the patient, or around both if the pain is in both, and move slightly upwards from the root of the ear after having marked the spot; and make X punctures around each ear; afterwards, treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	 of the mouth's torment
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 Torment that should be treated with cautery is only that which comes from fever, as we have said in the division of illnesses; and do not make cautery on those similar to those that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 When you treat this resemblance of torment that comes from fever of snakes and purges of the head and gargle, and if it does not work, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little above the temple, and the third between the two lips; and place the cautery in the part that appears healthy, and make a cautery on top of the ear slightly below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a finger; and leave the cautery until half the cheek is burnt; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And it resembles the cutaneous (one we have placed before), but it is a little more subtle and the knife should be a little larger; after curing the place as I said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 When apoplexy is chronic and you treat it as we have said, but there is no benefit and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on each temple of the head, one in the middle of the head, one in the place called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the opening of the stomach; and it should be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	 of lead
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient large pears and pills that purify the brain. Afterwards, wash the patient's head completely, and place a mustard plaster on the occiput as written in the treatise on plasters; and this is how to cauterize: do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 If it is healed in this way, good; and if not, make three cauteries in the middle of the head descending to the neck, with two fingers' breadth between each cautery; and treat as the others, and if you see a need, and the patient can endure, make one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two horns, and treat until it is healed; and let the cautery be called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	 of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	 It is necessary that the head be cleansed of hair and what we have said before; then wash the patient's head, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each horn, and one behind, and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient can endure, and the disease is severe, make four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it be until the most of the heart is burnt, and lift your hand; then treat until it is healed, and let the cautery be called "olivare" as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	 of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	 The epileptic should not use the cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first fortify the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section when the patient is strong and able to take medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, make him gargle and chew to fortify the brain often with good food; then raise his head in the middle, and there make the cautery as we have said before, and the cautery on the vein, and on each corner; and if the patient is strong and able, make cauteries as I have said for those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	 If the patient is a child, perform the subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	 When due to melancholy there are superfluidities or corrupt moistures and thick phlegm, then use these cauteries as we have said for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	 And if due to melancholy the superfluities incline towards melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him something to drink that will cleanse the brain, according to what is stated above in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After washing the patient's head, make a linen bandage well-formed like a circle and place it in the head. And let the patient sit cross-legged and be held securely from all sides; then apply the poultice, which consists of old sheep butter; and heat it over a moderate fire so that the two may suffer it; after emptying the circle inside the head, leave it to cool; and do this for the patient each week once with other good management until he is healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 And if you see many points being made throughout the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 This method of cauterizing moistens the brain equally; and then place wet cotton in butter and goose fat on it.
de l’awe des eulz	 of the eye's gaze
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	 When the gaze first comes to the eyes through the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something cleansing for the head, and protect it from all moisture, and make him sweat in the bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 Afterwards, instruct the patient to shave his head, and cauterize the top of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descent is in both eyes together, or one if the descent is in one; and during all the cautery, tie off all the veins and arteries that are under the skull, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; and beware of bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then staunch it with as much power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 Et je t'enseignerai en l'extraction des artères et à l'incision la précaution dont tu dois te préparer; et parfois, on fait une cautérisation ou incision sous les deux os derrière.
dou cors des larmes	 du corps des larmes
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 Et quant les larmes des yeux sont anciennes et habituelles et sont sur les veines, ou près des artères qui apparaissent à la surface du visage; et on voit que c’est une superfluité froide flegmatique, alors il fait le cautère dont j'ai parlé au début de cette opération descendante vers les yeux: un cautère dans la tête, deux cautères sur les deux tempes, deux cautères sous l’os, et s’il y a besoin de plus, alors il le cautérise prudemment dessus le sourcil à tout petit cautère.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	 From the body come tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	 When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient to drink for three nights cochies; afterwards, raise the head, and make a cautery in the middle of the olivary cautery; and make two cauteries of the cautery which is called "clavilis" on the two temples, one a little below the eyebrows; and beware of the artery lest you cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	 And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the membrane of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	 Pour cela il covient savoir la cause.
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 Car le feu cauteriue a tant de vertus qu’il est merveillous pour toute meintaine enfermeté.
dou poil qui point l’oil	 Et si tu veis que il les tient et ne s’en muet pas, ales tant que li sorcilz soient arses, et puis les remuet sans fainre aucune halte. ‍
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 Et se li oiel le poignent trop, si les metez en eau froide tant que il s’en sont estint.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 When they emerge and are equal, then place the patient in your care; afterwards, draw on the paper of the eyes a figure that resembles the leaves of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then place moistened cotton with egg white and muslin over the eye, then heat the cautery which has this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards, cauterize over the figure that you have drawn little by little many times, so that the hair is burned in that place; and the sign of the healthiness of the work is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised to the height of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for III days, then place moistened cotton with butter until the burn is removed; afterwards, continue the cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 And if after this the hairs come, and the skin is softened, then begin the cautery again on that same spot, as you did first; and if the hairs are lacking, then cauterize so that the skin is raised to its natural place, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 The cautery of burning medicine is such that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and even. Then make from parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one .З., and grind them together well. And do it quickly, so that it does not cool, then spread it on the form you have made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the skin of the eyes. And if the disease is in only one eye, one should work in one, and if in both, similarly. And put cotton moistened with egg white underneath the eye; and let the patient's eye be in your healthy hand, and place your finger showing on the medicine, and press the cloth and the egg white all the times that the patient feels the burning of the medicine, for he feels the burning as if by fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	 When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 And when the bite has passed, lift the skin of the wound, and look if you see the skin lifted as if it were lifted by the constriction of fire or by an incision; and if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If not, then put more medicine on the wound until your work is equal and your eyes are precise; then put cotton soaked in butter on it until the scab falls off; afterwards, cure the wound with ointment called «dyafenis» and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if you need to look closely at your work, do so with great care that no medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 And if the skin becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then begin the medicine again on that place which has been softened by the proper paper, as you have done before; then cure it until it is healed; and this is the shape of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 And know that the eyes of men are diverse in greatness and in smallness, and according to this be your restrictions; and do not answer the right way for him whose study is of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	 of the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	 When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments are not beneficial, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 Instruct the patient to put their head in your hand; and let the minister hold his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or lower his head; afterwards, place dampened cotton on the egg white or juice of parsley over the eye; afterwards, heat the cautery which is such: and it should be attached to the head like the shape of a feather quill, together with which is the cautery; if you see, let it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see, let it be like a tent; but nevertheless, this one that is shaped is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 Then press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, then open it, and draw forth the bow; afterwards, place a very hot cautery, and hold your hand to the cautery at the nose part above the eye, so that your hand does not falter; and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you approach the beginning of the cautery until the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 If not, then begin the cautery again one more time, and another if you need it, and let it be for three days; after that put moistened cotton with butter on it, and continue with the treatment of desiccating ointment until it is healed. And if forty days pass without healing, apply a corrosive medicine so that the bone may be exposed; and act according to what would come in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a method of cautery for fistulas that some of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 For a fistula, open the site; then place into the opening one subtle tampon made of what follows:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 and they make of the quantity of one pound; and hold your hand firmly in the camahan, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run to his eye; and it is necessary to place on the patient's eye cotton moistened with egg white or water: thus lead heals the fistula, and the sane through marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have spoken of, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, then it is necessary to administer a perforation to the nose, and to bring the fistula back into the body of the nose according to its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	 cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	 Mouth sores often occur on the lips, which are called "hair", and also on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	 When you treat these sores as we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not benefit, then heat a small scalpel-shaped cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place it quickly in those sores until it reaches the root; afterwards, treat the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	 of the throat abscess
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or in the eye, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after causing decay and rotting and being inflamed, it becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not benefit: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterwards, open or pierce the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron reaches to the bottom of it, and in the rear place; and do this once or twice, afterwards treat as we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is treated thus, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the rotten bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	 Of tooth movement
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it does not help, then place the patient's head in your lap; afterwards heat the cautery which will be described later in such a way that you put a reed on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; afterwards lift your hand and repeat the cautery according to your wish; afterwards have the patient rinse his mouth with salt water, and let it sit for an hour and spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	 And in this way the tooth that was moving is strengthened, and the softened gum is restricted, and the moisture that was causing decay is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	 Of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 When the pain of teeth comes from cold, whether it is in the cold or the heat, and medicinal treatments are not effective, then there is need for cautery in two ways: with a hot iron or with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 The cautery with wax is done thus: take wax from a cow and put the tip into an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a lance, and moisten it in boiling wax, and place it on the painful tooth quickly and hold until it cools; and do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth. And if you see that wool and cotton are moistened in cold wax, place it on the painful tooth, and put a hot iron on it so that the fire reaches the completion of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 The fire-cautery is such that you take a metal rod of iron or copper, and it should be thick enough so the smoke does not reach the patient's mouth; then heat the cautery, from which the form will come next, and place it on the tooth and keep your hand there until the cautery is cooled; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good butter during this cautery, and then he should rinse out strongly; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	 And make a cautery on whatever tooth you wish, according to what you are able; and this is the form of the rod:
des scrophules	 of the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the scrofula are of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not responsive to digestion by medicines, then heat the iron cautery as described below, and let it have two openings for the smoke to escape; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess. And if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; then place a wet cotton cloth soaked in butter until the burn is removed; afterwards cure the place with onions and bandages until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The shape of the wound:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 When the moistures rise up in the veins of the throat, and especially when this comes from a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the patient first be emptied by purgative medicines; afterwards, apply cautery to the root of the throat, and be careful not to go all the way to the throat, and burn only for a moment.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then perform another cautery at the junction of the neck with the top of the spine, and let the cautery be called "clavicle" as we have described before; and treat the place as we said before until it is healed.
de la toust	 from the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 When the cough and disease of the throat are from cold moistures, and the patient has neither fever nor dryness, and the disease is chronic, then perform two cauteries on the breastbone in close places; and another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts; and let the cautery be called "clavicle" according to the form that was said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 Et si tu veux, fais un cautère en piquant tout le long du point qui est appelé «poinçon» pour former ce qu'il y a au-dessus dans la maladie des oreilles; et que les points soient jusqu'à trente ou environ.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 Après avoir traité l'endroit selon ce qui a été dit précédemment, et que le cautère soit à trois rangées selon cette forme.
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	 Et parce que les cautères sont plus légers, donc tu en fais trois à la fois.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	 De la dislocation de l’épaule
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	 Lorsque l'articulation de l'épaule est luxée en raison d'une cause humide, et qu'on essaie de la remettre en place mais qu'elle ne peut pas rester, et qu'elle revient aussitôt à sa position désalignée avec de légers mouvements qui se produisent, comme nous l'avons expérimenté, alors il est nécessaire que tu réduises d'abord la dislocation.  Pour cela, utilise un appareil approprié pour appliquer une traction douce et continue sur l'articulation.  Assure-toi également de stabiliser le reste du corps pour éviter tout mouvement brusque qui pourrait aggraver la situation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 Afterwards, have the patient lie on his back and on his side; then lift the skin that is inside the tickling with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated within, heat up the cautery that has two nerves like this.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 And cauterize the skin until it reaches the side, and there will be four figures of cautery together with three cauteries; and because this is done with the three-nerve cautery, therefore the figures of cautery are six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tendon, and this is the form of the three-nerve cautery:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	 And sometimes it is placed on this one nerve, which makes eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 After, apply the cautery by burning with a hot iron; after that, make the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated above, which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thick part of the shoulder blade, or make many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 Because the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When in the stomach come coldness and much moisture that they draw out his complexion, and he has many catarrhs, and with the accustomed ways of cures he does not benefit at all, then it is necessary that the patient be seated on his back, and stretch out his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 For this, he makes three cauterizations. One under the sole of the foot by the quantity of a finger, all of the cautery closed, and two cauteries on each side so that the shape of the cauteries is at three angles, with such space between one and the other that they are not joined together when they release pus; and let the cauteries be so deep that they reach the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without deviation:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and he who will have fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and signing on the stomach one point according to the quantity that you wish from within; then cauterize all the cautery which is called "point.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the healing of the previous treatment, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	 When the liver has pain from cold and moisture and great flatulence, so that it is strongly displaced from its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and it does not help him at all, then the patient must be cauterized over his heart; and let there be 30 cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity over the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the ribs of a man come; and let there be the thickness of a finger between each cautery; and let the cauteries be long along the body, and do not press too much with your hand on all the cautery; and let only half of the heart be burned, and let the patient be upright on his feet; and if he cannot, then let him lie down, and let him extend his legs, and lift his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And if your intention is to cauterize these cauteries of the scalpel, if you are skilled and knowledgeable in the art, be careful not to burn the entire heart, for you would dry out the whole body; and do not go as far as boiling, for the heart is very delicate there, and know this for certain.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too severely; and if it is in the membrane, he feels insane pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And then, when this treatment should be done by the physicians, it is necessary that the patient be seated on his head; and then he should designate the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a grape, of which here is the shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 And cauterize with the cautery until the heart is burned, and it comes up to the spleen, until all the humors are expelled; after that, treat according to the treatment of the illnesses until they are healed; and it is not necessary that anyone other than one who has studied medicine for a long time use this cautery, for by whom fewer of these diseases have spread at any time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can work boldly, but nevertheless it seems to me that it is better to leave him alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	 of the pleurisy cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	 The ancients said that for pleurisy, one should use the cautery of the root of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia, the longest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your fingers; and soak it in oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize with the cautery between the sternum and the neck, and two small cauteries a little below in the part that is under the chin; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, slanting a little behind; and one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the sides of the chest opposite the cautery which is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand, but make openly as if sniffing.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And some ancients say that some men use a fire cautery resembling a razor, and heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches that abscess; and then the pain is relieved, as we have said in the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work there is danger that the patient may die immediately, or a fistula may form which cannot be healed.
