Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And the ancients called it "treatment for contusion," and it is that you do to the patient who has this disease the hairs that he may have on his forehead, then make III incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as II thumbs in the middle of the forehead going downwards until the neck, and the other two on the temples above the eyebrows, and beware of cutting the arteries that are on the temples above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the II jawbones, and let each wound be the quantity of III thumbs in width; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth for wiping away the blood, then apply the sharp spatula in two parts where this form is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	 From the incision which is in front of the temple up to the second incision; and scrape all the heart that is between the two slits at all the tissue that is on the bone, then do another part from the middle incision up to the other second, and then extract strongly this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	 If you put in the first slit the instrument which is called "scalpel," and it is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other; this is its shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And put the cutting side towards the tough heart tissue and the soft side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle slit.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it opens to the heart; then do another part in the middle slit up to the other defect; and then extract the blood equally, and press the place for the taken blood; then put in each slit a tent of old cotton, and put on wet cloths in wine and oil and vinegar, and ensure that such abscesses do not come there; and on the third day remove the bandage, and bring great plenty of warm water, then the cure of ointment basilicum with rose oil, and other cures by which wounds are cured, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	 Of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 When acute catarrh comes to anyone, and you see the eyes dim and small, and the vision weakened, and the eyelids burned; and the hair falls out, and there is a severe headache, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that those substances and this catarrh come from many veins, and if there is no cure for it, then this is the treatment.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And you should instruct the patient to shave his forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one as wide as an inch.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 And begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let the cut go down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when chewing; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then insert old cotton and linen threads between the two lips of the incision, then bind it with cloths soaked in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when they are removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that promote flesh growth.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	 In this manner: take two parts of flour from wheat, and four parts of resin, and make a poultice; and administer it in these wounds to heal all flesh.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 of the stoppage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	 Everything that falls into the ears is one of these four things: grain, an animal, a stone from mining or similar things like iron; or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils; or something flowing, such as water and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When something falls into the ear that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see the stone, then drip some drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze by conditioning [the air], and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upwards.  />
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Often fever comes from this treatment; if it does not come, then administer extraction with subtle lancets.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	 If fever comes from the lancets, it is good; if not, then administer extraction with a subtle onion of small double; and if it does not come that way, make an iron tube and insert the end of the tube into the ear canal strongly, and stop up what is around the tube with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the tube; then draw fever strongly, for very often fever comes as we have said; and if it does not come in this manner, then take a glutinous substance from which birds feed, and put some in a suitable instrument, and put a little cotton around; then press the glutinous substance on the stone or whatever it may be, and draw fever.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if she does not jump from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear before an abscess or spasm comes there; and the way of the cutting is such that you first make the patient sit under the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to its measure of virtue. Then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear into the fat or dependent place; and let the cut be like a half-moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it hastily to your mouth; and treat until he is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	 And if it is a grain that is inside and swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a subtle tenuous spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do this when you think the grain is moist because of the moisture in the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine tweezers and the suction cup, as we have said, so that the extraction may be easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 In the case where water falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use sneezing with pepper first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let him lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps out by itself, that is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If not by itself, then take many small and light stones according to the length of your thumb, and heat them slightly in the fire. Have the patient put one in the opening of his ear, and jump on his feet from the other side, and strike with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with stone after stone until all the water comes out, and thus it jumps out entirely. And if you see, then take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and hold the other end in the fire so that the thinnest part of the reed is burned; then repeat the process with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	 En l’estraction de la beste, if it is of small size, such as a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, then use extraction by pricking; and this is the lightest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	 En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in dealing with distillations, if the treatment does not help, then you must look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, draw them out with subtle pricks, and if they do not appear, take the cane of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And put the most subtle end in the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then suck all the wax out; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not come out, then stop up the ear with cotton as I have said before; and if they do not jump out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven for the killing of worms, and you will find in the treatment of distillations; and also distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this apparatus, which is shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	 And let it be of silver or brass narrow at the bottom with a small opening, and open on top for distillation; and to press in the distillation there is a well-made brass instrument for this purpose, and if you wish, take a scraper and wrap cotton around the tip evenly; then throw your oil or juice, and whatever you want of your medicines into the ear, and let the ear be in the ear; then put the scraper inside all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled into the opening of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be a little heated by the fire before you distill it into the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of the stoppage of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 No child is born without any hole in the ears; and this same thing happens to men by stoppage of a wound, or of flesh born within the ear, and these stoppages sometimes go deep into the ear so that it cannot be seen; and sometimes the hole disappears, which can be clearly seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 Therefore, those that go deep and cannot be seen are of serious illness in many cases, and in those that can be seen, it is necessary that you place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the stoppage clearly, then work with all this spatula to remove it.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	 Et il doit être aiguisé et tranchant à l'avant et à l'arrière tout autour, afin qu'il ne blesse pas l'oreille; si l'opération est sur la chair nouvellement formée ou le corps de l'oreille, alors tenez-le avec des pinces fines, et coupez légèrement jusqu'à ce que toute cette chair soit complètement enlevée.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the incision is deep in the ear, then take a subtle and light razor and heat it a little over the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the incision where the patient feels pain, pierce lightly and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and soak it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Do this every day until the wound is healed: Take a cloth and soak it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it. And if you see the ear swelling, then you must remove the cloth and apply another cloth moistened with ointment made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	 And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are described in the section on distillations.
de la char des papieres	 of the flesh of the blisters
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	 This blister that comes on the eyes when they are moist and then dry, you should extend it with tweezers and scissors, and cut off the top with a spatula made from its roots; then apply powdered vitriol to the place.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	 And if it exfoliates, then cauterize with the subtle lancet cautery, and after incision the cautery works well; and many times they return, because some part remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burnt and do not come back.
de la gresle	 of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Many times in the eyes there appear things that resemble hail in their shape and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hailstone", and it is a large assembly of moisture on the surface and inside the eye; the treatment is as follows: take care if the hailstone moves from one side to the other, which is an easy thing to know; then make a wide incision, then lightly scrape each part, then take it with forceps, and cut it off.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot cut it without piercing the skin a little, it does not harm the patient; and if the wound is large, sew it with one stitch, and cure it until it heals; and if it is small, do not apply too much pressure, for the ointment restores it quickly and heals the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	 And if the boil descends inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn the skin over and spread out the boil with tweezers, and cut and press it from both sides; and if the skin is pushed away by the incision, that does not matter; and when the boil is cut open, wash the area with salt water, and treat the place with that which heals flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	 of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 of the paper that is applied on top of the skin above it, and this happens more in children than in any other people, and it greatly troubles their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason, they always lie down on their faces and sleep with them, and their skin underneath their eyelashes is moist where the swelling and appearance are covered by exinach which opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press on the place with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	 And the manner of working is that the patient puts his head in your hand; and then take a cloth of linen, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach from each part, then put it on him; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered into the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp lancet a slit wide enough, and not be larger than the wound made in the vein of the arm; and pierce the skin deeply until you reach the exinach; and in many dispositions comes out exinach from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 Tear off then all in one piece of cloth between your fingers toward the outside, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is spread out; and beware that you do not approach the crack, lest you come to blind the entire eye up to the eyelid, lest you injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 And if the eyelash does not open at the beginning of the fissure, then widen the fissure slightly until it opens; then tear off as we have said, then moisten cloths in oil and water, and place on the spot, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And there are such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat until healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the boil is hot in place, then treat with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	 of the hair follicles
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 When hairs grow in papillae other than the natural ones, and they are irritated, they harm the eyes and bring on various diseases such as chronic tears, softening of the skin, and cataracts, to the point that it causes blindness; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by purgative medicine as described in the previous chapter on cautery, or by incision and suturing, or by canthus, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 It is necessary that you place the patient's head in your hand, then turn the paper of the eye towards your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; if not, insert a needle with all its thread on top; and let it be near the edge of the paper where the hair grows near these hairs, and draw the thread above all the way to the paper, and turn to the razor; then make an incision in the part below the paper, below the joined hairs, covering everything from the large tear duct to the small one; then extract the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and linen under the paper, then seal on the paper a figure of ink, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you wish to raise the paper which is divided for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And so, for one who needs it, cut a large quantity of the skin according to how soft the skin is; then make an incision along all the spatula lines that you have marked, and begin from the great tear duct down to the small one; let one of the fissures be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root; then put the ointment in one of the two corners of the heart; then remove all the skin; then join the two lips with a stitch of a needle at one thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make the superfluity of the threads adhere on the two sorcerers with any gluey things if you wish to do this; and if not, then don't worry about it, but leave the stitch and the threads for three days or four; then heal the wound without a stitch with drying and constricting substances, because the skin will heal on its own at the closing of the wound and the joining together, but the stitch is harmful (as the ancients say), and this work is without fear; and there is another way: which is to mark the skin with a figure that is like the leaves of myrtle, as we have described, with three open ointments according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	 then take this which surmounts the small forces equally according to the form that is here
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 and if you do not have the power to hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread, and push it into the figure; and push another thread next to the large lip, and the second thread next to the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have signed, as we have said, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if pus forms at your incision, soothe it with wax and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hair of the skin is turned: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but stitching in one place or another is more skilled.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	 Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: and the treatment of dogs is as follows: you must turn the paper and the opening inside as I have said; then make two dogs by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and as wide as the spatula's width; and cut off at the two ends where you hold the threads; then subtly connect one to the other above what surmounts the paper of the eye, and tighten the two dogs from the two parts firmly; and leave it this way for some days, and the skin that is tightened will die and blacken and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it delays, cut it with scissors, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the paper is removed, the hairs will no longer grow; and these are the shapes of the two dogs that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	 The work is such that you should take a subtle needle and thread it with a soft and subtle silk thread; then bring the heads together and tie them both subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange another brief thread of silk in the shaft, and tie the ends of the thread; then have the patient put their head on your hand; and let it be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is a subtle and small work.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	 And if the hair is removed and the hair does not come out with it, then you will draw out the hair all the way to the end of the thread that you have threaded, until the hair comes out through the hole above and you see it with your eye; then you will pull out the hair and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair regrows in its place and the flesh grows back; and if the hair is small, let there be one long natural hair accompanying it, and raise it with that one until it is elongated and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	 of the eye infection
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease called "aleacrati" or eye infection occurs in the eye, there are two types: one is natural, and the other is unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting, or from cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And the manner of working on it is that you split that joint, and sever its lips, and place linen tents inside, and bind it until it heals; and it is not necessary to use in its care things that dry out and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and wash it with water or altea, and seeds of flax cooked, and onions of dyacilon melted in some oils, and wrap a tent around it, and cure it this way.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	 And the treasure of your care is that you take heed that it does not heal according to the form which it was before; and these works which we have said are not beyond the remedies of this sickness, that it may return according to the form which it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	 of the flesh which comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This sickness that is beneath which is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from wound and tear and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you take a needle with which there are two threads, and the point into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left corner of the eye to the right, so that the thread comes into two corners of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and cut off one broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the shape of the stone returns as it should be, that is good; but if not, take a scraper and place it in the cleft, and turn the stone, and make two clefts on either side inside the stone; and let the heads of the two clefts be at the two corners of the incision that you have made, and let an angle be made so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter which is called "I grieche"; then remove that flesh according to the quantity that its edges are sharp beneath it, from what follows the stone, then join the two severed parts, and sew them with a wool thread; then follow the cure as we have said about softening medicines, and of tents, until he is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	 Et si la maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, il est nécessaire que tu fasses une incision pleine sous les poils des papiers; ensuite, tu dois faire l'opération selon la forme de la maladie, car elle est très diverse en forme. Et le sage maître doit préparer un ingénieux dispositif avec tout son pouvoir pour ramener la figure à sa forme naturelle; et le patient lui-même doit être préparé avec les instruments nécessaires en plusieurs positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	 Si la maladie vient de fendure, de couture ou de cautérisation, il est nécessaire que tu fasses une incision pleine sous les poils des papier
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When this fusion happens to some men in such a way that the skin above is fused with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor underneath the skin, and lift it up; and you apply the tweezers, until you cut what is in contact with the thin spatula, which should not be too sharp or cutting, so that the patient cannot tolerate being cut by the spatula; and your incision, with which you scrape off that assembly, should be light, so that the skin returns to its natural form; and all that assembly is healed, and sometimes in the eye it causes salty tears, and you lift it with fresh water, and with collyrium; then place between the skin and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye wool moistened with plenty of egg; and after three days use the collyrium and healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	 of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	 Know that the nail is in two forms: one is nerve-like and resembles a hard shapeless mass, and the other which is not nerve-like, but resembles white congealed moisture; when touched by iron or tried with pincers, no one can grasp it. Both appearances begin towards the inner corner of the eye, and grow little by little until they cover the entire sight, the light, and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	 And the method of incision is such that the patient places their head in your hand, then opens their eyes. And you lift the skin to your hand, then roll the nail with small pincers and place it above; then take a needle, and put one hair from a horse, cow, or ox into it, and a strong thread. And double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, and pierce all the way through with the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and place it above, and shave to the root of the nail following the vein and the silk of the hair up to the head, then trim the remainder in the corner of the eye with a subtle spatula and small forceps, leaving the natural flesh in the corner of the eye so that tears do not come through the incision; sometimes the nails are only placed on the eyelid and on the thread, as we have said.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And see to it that the saliva does not touch the flesh and tear it, and that the prune seed is not punctured; and after the incision, put in the eye a little of boiled linseed, and made from lead into oil, and leave it until the next day; then heal as needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	 And if the nail is not fleshy and you cannot insert the needle and the hook cannot enter, often this appearance of a nail is treated with medicine; and as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, then work on the eye of the patient, and take a little light saliva in this manner:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	 And shave the nail carefully, and if you see that it does not diminish and the root approaches, then drip into the eye a drop made of lead and red ocher and sealed, and stuff the eye until the next day; then begin again the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If nothing stands in the way in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then begin again with the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	 And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear duct affects the eye with great harm, then suspend it at the corner, and cut a part of it but not all, so that no tears come into it; then drip into the eye red collyrium which is made of lead.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	 Of the flesh that grows over the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 Of the flesh that grows over the eyelid, in some men there sometimes grows red flesh, which covers the eyelid and extends onto the cheeks and turns outwards, and it appears like a rose on a baluster; and the operation is such that the patient places his head in your lap, then you open the eyes, and peel off all of that flesh with tweezers suitable for this purpose, and hold it firmly; then cut off the first piece of flesh, and continue cutting to the root until the end, and be careful not to damage the eye during the operation; and let the incision of the spatula be as we said in the incision of the nail and small forces from which one removes the scab, as the figure after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, fill the eye with boiled salt water or instill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines into it, and place a cotton pad soaked in egg white on the eye, so that it is secure from inflammation; and if there remains anything, and pus overcomes you, and you doubt inflammation, then leave the eye and treat the inflammation with soothing remedies; then return to your operation until it is healed, and do the same when flesh grows in the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	 But nevertheless, you must cure each weak eye according to its natural way; and for the accidental way, in ironwork; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member can endure this work.
des voines des eulz	 of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 There are red veins that appear on the eye and prevent it from working properly, weakening the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 It is therefore necessary that you first check whether the eye in which there is a vein is sound and does not have any other disease except for the vein; then deal with the eye in this way: instruct the patient to place his head in your hand, then carefully cut those veins along the entire length according to your skill, and let the scissors be sharp, double-edged like this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	 Et que ce soit fait en deux fois, progressivement dans le corps selon cette forme :
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	 and then close subtly those veins with the forces, and wipe away the blood hour by hour until you see those veins withdraw from the eye; and take care not to injure the eye with the points of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very careful in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, then instill into the eye a green and red collyrium to destroy what remains of the blackness.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	 And if you do not have the power to close all of them in that hour, then make a poultice on the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and assured without infection, then begin again according to this manner which was before until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	 of the eye's fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	 The doctors call «arissati» fistula: when you cure it by cautery and with burning medicine as I have said before, and if it is not healed, there is an abscess within it that you should open above the abscess where it must die, and draw out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	 And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then clean it with all the tools of which this form exists; and it is called «aspre chief», and let it be made of iron or steel, and let it be sharpened like a file as shown in the present figure:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	 And place the corrupt bone under the healthy one, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand until you know that this corruption is dried out; and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 if the place is healed and flesh grows there, and the body of the wound is healed and remains so for forty days without reopening or becoming infected with evil accidents, then you know that it is healed; but if not, there is no other device than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nostril in this manner: and it is necessary that you expose the bone a second time with iron and sharp medicines, and when it is exposed, take a piece of wood like this shape, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the stick be thinned until its end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 Then place it on the bone near the eye socket, and remove your hand from the pocket, then turn the drill completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because the wind exits if he holds his hand over his nose; and then restore the place with dry medicine, as I have shown you, and when the flesh emerges and hardens the place, the material goes to the nose; so it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	 of the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the eye is completely open throughout and there is no obstruction or shrinkage of the nose, it is necessary that you bind the patient; then heal it, then place cupping glasses on the temple without pricking to draw out, then place on the eye a plaster made of alum, aloe, frankincense, and mastic, then hold the eye, and bandage with cloths and strips; and the manner of the cloths is such that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one four times, and then place one on top of the other according to the amount that the eye needs; then bind tightly above with a firm strip, and renew the cupping glasses to draw out without pricking; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the bandage softens, it is necessary that you bind it strongly; then remove the bandage after the day and night, and if you see the eye begin to heal, it is good; if not, then renew the plaster and the cloths and the bandage and the cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	 For the breaking of a bladder swelling
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 When disruption occurs in the bladder swelling, it opens, and there comes out pus like grains of resin, which is frightening to see; then if you see it open, the operation is such that you insert a needle into the root of the lower part until it reaches the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the edge of the eyelid; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the position; then cut off the place of the double thread and tie a piece of the bladder around it, and tighten it well, then extract the needle and put on the eye a cloth moistened with plenty of egg; and let it be until the threads join with the bladder, then treat the eye with soothing things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restricted by the bladder each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the eyes give off a strong appearance, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes to the depth of the eye, and drain the watery moisture, and let the eye descend, and insert it quickly; then draw it out until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	 from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing other than water that is gathered in the eye, appearing like descending water, and this is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move it so that you see the water come above your eyes; then let it be inserted, and do not allow it to descend and let the light be obstructed, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the water is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If the patient is sitting between your hands, then take a fine spatula and make an incision on the horny layer of the eyelid along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horny layer and the cornea, until the abscess comes out; and when it has come out, drip hot water mixed with honey into the eye, or boiled fenugreek water mixed with honey, then continue treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	 of the water of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have seen similar waters in the division, and those that should be pierced; then operate according to good health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and tie the healthy eye tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand if the eye is right; then place the point of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a hair at that shiny part of the eye towards the inner corner, then thrust the instrument called "almagda" skillfully, and turn your hand until it pierces into the shine of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the empty place; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda be to the depth of the measure of the space from the pupil to the end of the black; and this is the cornea of the eye; then you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the horny layer, and then place the instrument up to where the water is, then press down one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If the water descends now, then the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After resting it a little, and if the water rises again the second time, place the finger with the instrument, and when it is inserted and does not rise, gently withdraw the almond turning your hand a bit; then put back in water a drop of holy oil, and lift the eyelid inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then place over the eye cotton or wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg yolk, and bind with clean cloth.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, apply comfrey with plenty of egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the almond cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have eyes that are too hard, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", which looks like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make the place subtle; then put in almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient an agreeable sleeper, in which he should sleep on his back in a dark place; and be free from all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and let him be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in that same dark house, and test his vision, and show him some things, and then rebinding him until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the time of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you bind him beforehand, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If abscesses like this appear, uncover the eye before the seventh day, and apply what relieves abscesses; and when it is calmed, uncover the eye and place on its face a bandage for some days, and let it always be in that darkened room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then go out of the house little by little, and turn according to his case; and know that no disciple should interfere in this matter.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	 And one came to us who was from Iraq, who told us that in his country they make an almagda, at which water is drawn out, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing. ething
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	 And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them may see them; and they should be made of pure brass.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	 And their heads should be of the same subtlety, and their ends in three sharp points.
de la char sor le neis	 on the flesh of the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes there are various flesh growths on the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are those of this kind where there is reddish flesh, and there is soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In that case of this flesh which is soft and not reddish, you should have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and work their nostrils, and apply the salve to those growths, and draw them out; then cut off what you can sustain with a subtle sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all of the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 And if there remains anything that cannot be cut out, then open it all with subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if it overcomes you, or if it is an abscess, then support it as needed; and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize until the pus is dried up and all the flesh is removed, then throw into the nose easily and with vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the nose swells, and moisture reaches as far as the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not break through as needed, know that there is new flesh born on the bone above, which prevents the instruments from cutting: then it is necessary that you put a thread of linen in, rather thick, and knotted by hand, and between each knot there should be a finger's width or less; and let the patient hold the end of the thread in his nose with all his might, and draw it through to the point where it comes out of the nose into the mouth; and many times children do this in school, and it is an easy thing for someone who wants to do it; then hold the end that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and pull one after the other, tightening like us who are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do this as long as you know that the nostrils have corrupted that flesh, then remove the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose again as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has dissolved all that remains of the flesh; and then put a stick of lead into the nose for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to clean out the head, in which one distills the oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 And let it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and its passage similarly; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full for cleaning out the head; and let there be one handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	 of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 Often there is on the tip of the nose a disease called "telul", and it grows and becomes very large, so that it is a visible thing to look at; and for this reason you must cut it at the beginning, and remove all of the hard substance, then place on it the cautery or burning medicine; and if one waits to cut it until it is large, then beware if it is hard, of foul color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is a hidden abscess, for when one cuts it sometimes, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of foul color, and you see that it can be completely cut, then let the patient bleed and cut without fear, and treat the place with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	 When the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
