Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, when this happens to someone, look first if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips in one stitch, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, it is necessary that you cauterize all the parts of their heart until they heal, then join the two lips in one stitch, and hold them, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood and crushed incense; and put a piece of strong emplaster or other adhesive plaster on the powders, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then cure with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	 The manner of the suture is such that you join the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	 of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	 At many men there happens within the lips a hard abscess, similar to grains of peas, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lip, and cut into each bump, and take it with tweezers and chop it in every part; then fill the place after the incision with vitriol powder, until the flesh is stained; and then apply aloes leaf, and cure the place with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	 of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 Many times a growth appears on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; then you must hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run out; then place vitriol powder, or other restraining and desiccating powders, on the spot; and if that growth returns after the incision, which often happens, then cut it a second time and cauterize it: it will not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	 of the growths
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 Sometimes there are growths at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth turn black and yellow, to the point that the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become putrid; then you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and scrape off the teeth or growths until nothing remains; and do likewise with the blackness and greenness, and the yellowness and other stains, until they are cleaned away; and know that the teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work demands, because the scrapers used on the surface of the teeth have different shapes than those used between the teeth; and these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	 It is necessary that when you treat the tooth for its pain, you delay pulling it as long as possible, because no one should do this; because it is a very high substance up to the point where there is no excuse for pulling it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is forced to pull [the tooth], you must be certain of the tooth that hurts.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the pain deceives the patient and thinks that it is in a healthy tooth, and has the good tooth pulled out; and nevertheless the pain does not depart from this until the evil one is extracted, because we have already seen this happen with these lords; and when you are well certain of the hurting tooth, then you must cauterize all around the tooth to ward off the gum on all sides; then move it with your fingers or with fine pincers tooth by tooth, until they are well loosened, then firmly hold the pincers; and let the patient's head be in your lap between your knees, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and push it gently on each side, and remove it as you first did.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is perforated and eaten away, then you must fill it with dressings in the places where the openings are; and delicately clamp it with tongs so that it does not break when clamped; and you must work very skillfully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And beware well that you do not break it, and a part remains, and the patient suffers greater pain due to the root's wickedness than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware that you do not act like the ignorant healers, who in their haste and boldness sometimes break the tooth, and do not bring what we have mentioned; but sometimes cause a great disease through the roots that remain, or because of the tooth they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood flows from it, which often happens, fill the place with powdered vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	 The shapes of the instruments, to which one attaches the teeth first, should be long and thick, so that they do not double when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	 And let them be of large members so that they do not bend at all when drawn, and let them be made of good iron, and let them have teeth to hold well.
de la racine des dens	 from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains after extraction, it is necessary that you place cotton moistened in butter on the spot for one day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the spot is softened, then insert the tongs called "algefri", making the tooth resemble a beak; and let them be made inside like a file, and this is its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, it is necessary that you uncover all the flesh around the root and place the instrument called "althali", which is also known as a chisel, in its form.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	 Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, and if the root jumps out like this, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments, from which the forms come afterwards.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	 And so one helps oneself with this instrument which has two handles, of which there is the form here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	 and other irons that are in front for the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tongs, of which there is the form here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	 And let this instrument be strong so that it does not break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and likewise other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise master finds his own instrument by himself, according to what his work and the disease show him, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their differences, and if one does not break the cartilage or other bones, then he looks for the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and helps with the gestures, of which there is the form here:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	 And let them be thick and well-anchored to hold the bone, so it does not slip but can be held and removed; then restore the place with appropriate medicine, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, raise it all with this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	 When the teeth appear not according to nature, and their shape is ugly, especially in young women, you must know if the tooth is new after the teeth have erupted, and it is not in its right place, and one cannot pull or grind it: then remove it; and if it is above the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a little beak, made of iron, sharp at the top.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	 And the blade cuts little by little each day due to the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that one can be filed down, then file it with a file of this kind:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	 and it is also like the file with which needles are made; and file the tooth little by little each day gently, so that it does not move until it falls out; then in the end flatten it with any scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and injures the tongue, it is necessary to file down the roughness until it is level, so that it does not injure the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	 when the teeth become loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the front teeth are dislocated, either by impact or falling, and the patient cannot press on what he bites without them falling out, and you have treated them with restricting medicines, but it doesn't work; then they need to be restricted with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never moves; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the eyes between the crooked teeth, whether there is one or several, until you wisely reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again up to the part where you started, and subtly and wisely tighten your hand so that they do not move; and let your thread be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, and then place them between the healthy teeth,
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 And when the tooth falls out, replace it in its place, gradually as we have said; and do not interfere with this if you are not wise and patient, and sometimes one makes a form of a cow's bone tooth, and puts it in the place where there is a lack, and secures it as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	 of copper the wire of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Often this wire comes from under the tongue either by nature or by injury from a healed wound; and the operation is such that you open the patient's mouth and place his head in your lap, then lift the tongue; then cut the nerve wire wide, so that the tongue is dislocated from its position, and if there is hardness or knot, which is from the sudden closure of a wound, then insert the hook and cut the wire wide; and be careful that the slit is not too deep for the artery underneath; and when you have done this, lift the area with rose water and aloe, or cold water, then place a linen cloth under the tongue; and let the patient wash the site every night, so that it may not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if the flow of blood comes, then place vitriol powder on the spot; and if the blood continues to flow, then cauterize with the cautery called lentigo, which is good for this; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it turned to the color of soot or black or hard, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer; and if it tends toward greenness, and there is moisture, then apply alum, and make a hole with a subtle spatula, and remove it from one side and the other; and if the blood continues to flow during your work, then place vitriol powder on it until it becomes blackened, then return to your work until you have drawn out all the force; then lift up the spot with silk and linen, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	 of the throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes there appear in the throat boils which are called "godath", and they are properly called II almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small sense and of pus color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the flow of blood; but leave it until it dies, and then you will divide it, or it would burst by itself; and if it returns to white color, and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument for covering, but first check if the abscess is hot and quiet.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and his head should be in your hand, and he opens his mouth and you take the instrument between your hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument, of which there is this form; and it should be of silver or fine tin as sharp as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 And when you press the tongue down with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the onion and stick it in the almond, and draw it out above as much as you can; and draw something from the cloths along with it, then cut off the instrument, of which there is this form, that resembles tweezers; and nevertheless the tips are curved, and one next to the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or adamant:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	 Et si tu n'as pas cet instrument présent, emprunte-le aux tenailles, dont voici la forme :
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 Et soit tranchant d'un côté, et nommé d'autre part; et quand tu as coupé l'une des amygdales, coupe l'autre de la même manière, puis après l'incision, rince la bouche du malade avec de l'eau chaude et de l'eau salée. Si du sang sort, alors rince la bouche du malade avec de l'eau où des écorces de pommes grenades ou des feuilles de myrte ont été cuites, jusqu'à ce que le saignement s'arrête; ensuite soigne jusqu'à guérison; et parfois d'autres abcès apparaissent dans la gorge à côté des deux amygdales, alors coupe-les aussi de la même manière.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that had grown within her throat, specifically the small gland; and it had nearly closed off her entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she remained this way for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess had risen so high that it had pushed out two ribs through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I hastened immediately and inserted a small needle into one of the nostrils, then pushed it through, and drained a large amount of pus; then I did the same in the other nostril, opening the mouth and pressing the tongue; afterwards, I inserted the needle into the abscesses and drained some of it, but only a little blood came out; thus the throat passage of the woman was opened, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess always regrew, filling the place that I had emptied, until it became very large again; then I placed a device in it and cauterized it within the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and knew only that God would do with her after me.
de l’uve	 of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When pus descends into the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large, and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that this abscess has subsided, and it is subtle, then you must cover it; and the one which is round in shape and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a dark color or black, then you must avoid incising into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 Because there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it according to the manner that I have said, of its color and length, let the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the hook into the eye and draw it downward, and cover it with the two instruments that I mentioned for the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you not cut more than the excess which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, then it harms the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the II almonds, and treat until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being cut, then you must use an ingenious method to calm their fear during the cauterization.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the method of cautery is very sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And it is that the patient places their head in your hand, and then presses the tongue against the instrument which we have said in the chapter on cautery, and cauterize with lively water like this, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, whose form is thus:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And let there be on the head a tuft where one places the medicine, as the strands of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and the patient should lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not descend to the throat, and wounding it; then hold your hand with all the medicine and press on the eye, for the duration of half an hour, until you see it become numb and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and push the instrument with all the cotton into the tear duct above, until the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is perfected, then let it dry, and after four or five days it will fall off. And if you need to restart the cautery of the medicine, then restart it, and after the cautery, wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and let it be rinsed with cold water, and let it be cured with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 This cure is more skilled than the incision or the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and oregano and rue and camomile and lavender and similar herbs, and assemble all of them or some of them in a pot, and put ashes therein, and boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot let there be an instrument shaped thus.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 It should be made of silver or brass, and one end of it should be inserted into the patient's mouth until the vapor reaches the eye through the nose, until the eye is weakened; then repeat often, until the eye dries out. Be careful not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, because many things can happen; and it should not be done unless at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this instrument is not present, take a reed and place inside it the crumb of an egg, so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot; for the egg crumb does not allow the steam to irritate the mouth, and this is a good cure along with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 Many times a bone or fishbone gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press the patient's tongue against the instrument, so that you can remove the object; and whatever does not open and is lodged in the throat, you should make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the hard thing will come out with the vomiting; or the patient may swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of flax, or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out with what we have said, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 And let the instrument be curved at the tip so that it may more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted upwards; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest the throat swell or break a bone inside; and it is better that the patient himself puts in the instrument, because he will be more accustomed to such things; thus he pushes it downward, where he draws it strongly with all the instrument equally until it is strong.
de la sansue de la gorge	 of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the blood is treated, as I have said in the division, by the healing of medicines; and when this does not work, then look at the patient's throat in the sunlight after you have pressed the tongue with the instrument that I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see blood, draw it out with a very small hook or fine pincers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if this does not work, take a hollow reed, and put it in the patient's throat, then insert a hot iron into the reed's hollow, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient is feverish all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 then take a full glass of cold water, and hold it in your mouth, and pour it into the throat without swallowing, and move it around with his hand often; and as soon as the blood feels the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall out as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument I mentioned for the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And the manner of fumigation is such that you take a pot with glowing coals, and let it be covered by a cloth pierced in the middle, and through that hole place the head of the instrument; then cast your fumigation, and the patient places the head of the cane in his mouth, closes his mouth so that no smoke escapes, but it comes to the blood vessel; and the blood vessel will fall immediately, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and such, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	 And the shape of the instrument with which one draws blood is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved pincers to enter the throat; and it should have the appearance of a hawk's beak, and there should be roughness like a file, so that what it takes, it cannot leave; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	 the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 There are many kinds of abscesses, as will be remembered hereafter in this book and others, and they are different in penetration and cutting; and this is in two ways: one is in its own appearance, and the other because it retains moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 Because the abscess of the head is different from that of the base, and the fleshy abscess is different from that which occurs in joints, each should be judged according to its nature in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And there are abscesses which one should not pierce until the head is ripe according to its development; and there are those which must be pierced when they are hardened, and do not ripen according to their nature, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when an abscess comes near a joint, and it is left until it rots all around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 When the abscess is near the main member, and if you delay the perforation until it is dead, it will harm the main member; when it is near the anus, pierce it as soon as it is dead; and it is not necessary to pierce a mature abscess before digestion is complete, except for one that is near the anus, lest it become infected deep inside, and form a fistula; and may not heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	 It is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of a dead abscess according to its completion, and this is when the pain is appeased, and the separation of the fever, and the diminishment of the pain and redness, and the subsidence and maturation of the abscess head, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation sit in the most dependent place of the abscess, and where it opens more; and let the perforation be lengthwise along the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and near nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no pliability.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those (cases) where they bend, according to this member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it beforehand, the body will be filled with the abscess's poison, and it is full of much filth; and by chance the lips and depths of it may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is an abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary that you make small holes in small abscesses, and large holes in large abscesses, and many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where you need to make a cut, and cover (it) when they become like cloths, and are dead, then you should act as one does with carbuncles: and if there are those that are split into three angles, and if there are those which are capped as the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the armpits; and if there are those where a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Ceux qui n'ont point de chef, comme un furoncle superficiel, il faut que tu le perces entièrement; et lorsque le furoncle est gros et qu'il a formé une grande boule, et que tu le perces, ne tire pas toute la boule en cette heure, mais en retire une partie; ensuite, tamponne le furoncle jusqu'au lendemain, puis retire à nouveau quelque chose; fais cela plusieurs fois de suite, tant que toute la boule sorte; il en est de même si le patient est de constitution faible, ou une femme enceinte, ou un petit enfant, ou un vieil homme décrépit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 Because the spirit sometimes jumps out with the release of the pus, which may cause the patient to die unexpectedly, and you would not be aware of it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have noticed your abscess, wipe the wound clean, and look to see if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a simple cut, place cotton or old linen bandages over it; and if it is a large abscess and there are many openings, you must insert one bandage into each opening so that they come together; and if you have cut into the abscess and removed some skin, you must fill it with dry cotton or linen cloth scraps without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it and treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold and easy water, and wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, bring treatment and care, and the powders that I mentioned in less quantity in this book, and if it is in winter, and the place of the abscess is very sensitive, then you must apply wet tents and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the place is fleshy, then you must apply wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then release the abscess and dry and treat it, as needed, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	 And this must be known generally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	 from sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where small abscesses come from the head, and are like those that are in tissues, like the eyes of a hen, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that are fat and such that have moisture like pus; and there are those which are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the surgeon does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of the cut is such that you prove everything with an instrument called "spoon," from which the form comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Because if it contains moisture, then make an incision over the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is removed, then scrape off without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, because it returns again if anything is left there; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and oil, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day; and those who stay overnight will cure them.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then renew the cotton as before on the second day and the third, so that you are certain it does not remain overnight; then treat the wound with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess holds a knot of fat, cut it according to this form, lengthwise; and cast your onions upon it, and peel it from all sides, and put all your care into drawing forth the cloth where it lies; and if the art of healing goes against you, then do as I have told you afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do likewise for the abscess if it is pustulous, and in cutting and in dressing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cut into the pustulous and moist abscess, for it is more delicate, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if there are some of these abscesses at the head where there is no moisture, and such were the abscesses that I cut at the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck against it, one would have made as much a wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses coming to the head, except those which come to the heads of children and the roots of the ears, let the opening always be in the most dependent place so that the pus may exit; and treat it as needed.
des scrophules	 from scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 This abscess often occurs in the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin; sometimes it appears elsewhere on the body, and they are numerous and interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula is specifically within its rib, like the nodule and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similar to these scrofulae.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malignant and refuse to obey health. ‌
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In that case, then, which you see of good disposition for touching, and is similar to the color of the body, and moves from every part and is not harsh on the nerves of the neck or on the artery or on the canal, and is not deep; then you must cut it above, and scrape each part, and stretch the two lips of the heart at the corners, if you need to, as we have said in the case of head abscesses; and draw little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let the spatula not be too sharp or cutting, lest the hand slips, and do not go too far forward, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, then put into the wound vitriol powder, or some powders that staunch blood, and bind the wound; and let it be so until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the blood is staunched, then return to your work until you complete it; then check with your finger if there are any small scrofulous growths remaining, and cut them off and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous growth, then it is not necessary to cut this scrofulous growth at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and bandage it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut all the scrofula, it is necessary that you join together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 it is necessary that you cut the root of it and pull strongly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulae which retain excessiveness, pierce there where the wound opens; and pierce it in a similar manner as those previously mentioned, hanging downwards, then introduce tents with ointment and similar things, so that they corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, cure it with a rich ointment of flesh until it heals.
de squinance	 Of a dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	 The ancients spoke and discussed the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and this is written according to their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 For those who have dislocation, it is necessary that the slit of the throat called "epiglottis" be cut; and one should not help through this, because all the veins and the pommon of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	 When the illness is in the channel of the pommon, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid death from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it below three circles or four, a small slit across, between the two circles or by the amount of the siphon, not in the cartilage; and these places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no flesh there, and the vessels are long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is fearful, then it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to all the nape, then split the heart until it reaches the chin; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the hypoglossal nerve as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein of the chin which flows stronger through the broken place, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the hour has passed in which one fears strangulation, bring together the two lips of the heart wound and sew them up alone without a patch; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasis said that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dead, and his wing fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Therefore, cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the mischief of the disease has passed, which passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to close the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a young woman took a knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the cartilage of the larynx; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	 I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had flowed from it, although it had not struck a vein or artery except for the throat, and the wind was exiting strongly through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hastened and sewed the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and nothing more happened to the maiden except that she lost her voice, which later returned to normal; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	 of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in color like charcoal, and it is very common in women; and there are two types: natural, and accidental; where the natural type has no venom.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accident occurs in two ways, one is like our nose, and the other way is like an abscess that comes from us of artery; and there is fear, and it should not be worked on by making a hole except in that which is small, and test and search all around: if you find it as we know our nose, and it does not open to any vein, then cut it off, as one cuts the nose, and draw out all its hair, if there is any; and look well early on, and treat it as it should be, until it is healed perfectly.
des nous	 from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many kinds of nose are there, whose all resemblances I will tell; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between our (nose) and abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	 I say that it is cold and feverish, as long as the inflammation has passed, and putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With the new, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a sac, which is its own bag and according to the body's color, and begins like a blister, and grows; and they are in two types, either fatty or moist, and many of their colors are as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	 It is necessary that when you come to the treatment of the new [growth], you should first try and inquire about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire," according to its form, as it will be shown in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the manner of investigating abscesses from us is that you take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the intermission, and be careful not to jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If the moisture running out is of any color, puncture it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the intermission no more moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then puncture it in a cross shape, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape from each side and beware the wall where it lies that you draw it out whole with the thread; and if you cannot draw it out whole, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 Car if anything remains, the nose returns many times; and if a bit remains and the wound pains, fill the wound with some corrosive, burning powders, bind the wound, place on it things that calm the abscess, heat the abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the nose is large, sew together the two lips of the wound, and treat this as one would for an injury to the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	 And if the vein pulsates against you or another, then hasten and fill the place with powdered vitriol, and let it lie there for two days or three, so that the wound may suppurate and the boil of the blood subside; then return to cauterize what remains of the knot.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Here are the forms of the introducers, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are also three kinds: large, medium, and small, for encircling the abscesses of fistula; and they are like the needles with which one sews the sorceresses, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are worth more, and they are tried more in black lead to encircle the swellings of fistula; and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The forms of the onion are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; there are also onions that have two corners of three kinds as well; there are also onions that have three corners, and they are also of three kinds; and there are onions that have two corners, and onions of only one corner, and they are all necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The points of these are sharpened, and there are some that do not cut from both sides, which are used to remove the skin so as not to cut the vein or nerve; and among these instruments are the hooked lances held in handles, so that the patient does not notice them when opening abscesses; and they come in three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them except on fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and angles, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the peeling of chestnuts, according to this form, with which one stops bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	 And it is placed sometimes in the place that heals quickly with veins, and with arteries, and sometimes they return according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to become corrupt, so much so that they seem like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, it must be done according to this form of these lines b to g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine containing meat, then sew the two lips of the wound together, and care for it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs down and is softened due to its size as often happens in women, make two incisions above the two breasts through two similar slits, so that one is held by the other at the end of each, such that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from this line b up to this line g; then scrape off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about suturing and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely done because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with moistened cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it consumes the remaining fat, then care for it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	 of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	 This abscess which comes under the armpits is a kind of hard scrofula where there are ribs, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply an ointment suitable for this purpose until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if the abscess is like a scrofulous ulcer, cut it as we have said for scrofulous ulcers, and if the wound becomes pus-filled, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	 of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is cut and the skin above it is sewn up, abscesses often form; likewise with a swollen vein and an abscess; and one knows this when it is due to the artery, for then the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel constriction; and when it is due to the vein, there is often a lack of blood flow visible; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the nails or in the angles or in the neck or in many other places, for it is very large.
