Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, one must avoid the cure of iron, and he who is chief should also avoid it; and in that which is due to swelling of the artery, cut through the skin lengthwise; then make an incision at the angles, and carefully separate the artery from the veins until it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath it, and make it pierce through to the other side, and constrict the artery with two threads in three places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then pack the place between the two ties with a plug until the blood comes out, and let the abscess be relieved; then apply the dressing that covers the wound, until the threads fall off; then treat it as one would a burn, so that it heals; and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, you must dip your hand in what you can from the abscess all over the skin, then insert the needle underneath the place where you hold your hand, and make it pierce through, and there should be a double thread, so that you draw it out on the other side; then bind the abscess as I have told you, with one end of the two threads in two knots at the ends of the filament; and if you doubt that the threads will come undone, then insert another needle all along the thread underneath the entire abscess at the first incision, and constrict the threads in four places; then cut away the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut away the excess skin and leave what is bound; then apply a cloth moistened in wine and oil, then apply dressings of tenths and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	 of the abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	 Similarly, as an abscess comes to the artery and the vein, so it comes to the nerves when they are pierced, or by too great a labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more often in the shoulders and arms, and in all places where there are joints, and it is very painful, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in many positions without pain; and when one presses it strongly, the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely within the body, but beneath the heart; and it moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, or down or up, and that which is in the joints should not be struck with iron: perhaps contraction would occur; and that which is in the head or forehead, split the skin with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it by the corner, skin it, then remove and close the wound with stitches, and tend to it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	 of hanging swellings
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in the stomach and nowhere else, and this is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to them, and it has subtle roots and large heads; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his stomach that looked more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were always oozing moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I cut them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI, and the work in the incision is such that you observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is pale and moist with a subtle root; then cut it with a wide spatula, and let the cautery be present in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in cutting often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the wound overcomes you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient is frightened and fearful of the incision of iron, then take a well-made linen thread and bind the artelul as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to bind the linen thread until it cuts off the artelul, and each does its work without difficulty; and if the roots are thick, be careful when cutting, but you can cut half, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and take care not to cut the telul which is of red color and poor sense and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	 Car this is an ulcerated abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the ulcer later.
quant li boude ist fuer	 when the wound is strong
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the wound comes from a burn or a tear in the intestines, and it is on the abdomen and some of the other wounds are like this, as happens with other perforations, or from bleeding veins or arteries according to what was said before, or from flatulence; and if it is due to the perforation of the intestine and the exit of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a slight thing without pain, and it opens with various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	 And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is even more diverse, and when pressed between two fingers, it returns, and then comes back, and by chance it may harden, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and with great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and it opens well when you press it in your hand, do not constrain at all; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess opens with these signs: large and hard, and fixed according to a certain amount; and if it is due to windiness, then it is soft to touch, and the work is such that you should look to see if the appearance is of the blood from the artery or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 Then you must leave the treatment alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is of the intestine or bowel, then you must instruct the patient to hold his leg, and let it be stretched straight; then surround the entire thigh with a bandage; then command him to lie calmly between your hands, then go all around the place that you have marked with all the spatula, then extend half of the abscess above onto the large uncine; then tie it all around with a strong thread or a cord of thick silk firmly, and let the knot of the ligature be secure; then work the other half of the abscess stretched out on the ligature, and put your index finger in there, and search for the intestine; if you find it caught by the ligature, then loosen it, and push the intestine back into the belly; and if you find the bowel, then take hold of it with the uncine, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein gives you trouble, then go around well, then return to your work and take two needles, and put in two strong threads, and insert the two needles all around what you have done in a cross that you made perforate; then draw the abscess onto the needles in four places, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the place until it rots, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself; or you cut it when it has softened and rotted, then cure the abscess as we have said; and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as it should be cured, and close the place.
dou chancre	 Of the sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	 We have said in the division the resemblances of the sore, and how one should work on it with medicines, and how one should avoid the cure of iron; and we say the sore is in the flesh, and great care is needed in the cure, and the ancients said that when the sore is in a place where it can be scraped off, such as a sore in the breasts, and in the thighs, and similar places, one should remove all of it when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, one should not approach it, for I have never seen anyone healed from it; nor has anyone ever been healed from it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the work, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you first purge the patient of black bile; then make him fast if he has manifest repletion; then put the patient in a good place to do the work; then apply your fingers on the sore, and press from all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and compress the area well with your hand or any other thing, and if the bleeding bothers you from cutting into an artery or a vein, then cauterize until the blood is blackened; then cure it with another cure until he is healed.
de ydropisie	 Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have already said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: this is only for «eclites»; and one should not touch iron in these two similarities, namely tympanites and hypochondria, for it is mortal; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy called «eclites» with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, then consider whether the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as a swollen belly and similar things; then do not touch iron, for there is doubt. And if you see that the patient is of strong virtue, and he has no other disease but only dropsy, and he is neither too young nor too old, then proceed thus: lift the patient straight up on your hands, and have an assistant press the belly outwards, expelling the water to the lowest part of the foot, then take a thorny spatula according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut from two sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And at the point, and however it is not so deep that when you stick it in it may reach the intestines and wound them; then look to see if the dropsy is on the side of the intestines: then your cut should be above the navel on the right side below the wrist; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, let your cut be on the left side of the navel; and if it is due to urine retention, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lie on the incision so that the excess fluids do not run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push it through, and lift your hand to all the thickness between the skin and the flesh as if you were peeling to the extent of a nail or around; then pierce the flesh until the thickness comes to the desired place, which is the watery place, then draw out strongly, and into this instrument is put what follows:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it is similar to a fine silver wire, and it is made of light bronze or copper, and has in the lower part a small hole; and on one side there are three holes, and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a pen, and that is the shape of the incision with which the scribe cuts the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 On the top of this is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it immediately goes up on the instrument; drain then half or a third, for if you drain more than is necessary at that time, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit in blood, or he falls fainted, or approaches death; but drain according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and his pulses; then remove the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now by the cork that stops the hole that is on the still, as I have said, pierce in this manner; then renew the instrument the next day, if you see the patient tolerating this, and draw a small amount of water; do this every day, and be careful not to overdo it until only a little water remains.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and you leave much water in him, cure him with burial or hot sand, and through much sweating or bathing in the sun, and dye him with wine; and cure him with desiccative medicines until he is dry, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	 Of the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born without a hole in the penis, or with a small hole, or with it not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 Then it should be pierced immediately if it has no opening, and must be done very skillfully according to this manner:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 And then put into the hole a subtle plug of lead, and tie it and hold it thus for three days or four, and when he wishes to make urine, let the plug be removed, and make urine, and then replace it; and by chance it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 He whose hole is small, let him be treated with the lead plug as we have said, and it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 He whose hole is not in its place is injured, for some are born with the hole at the head of the penis, which prevents them from urinating unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot have sex because the matter cannot reach the testicles, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the manner of the work is such that the patient often lies on his back, then stretch the head of the rod and the handle similarly to the width of a pen, so that the hole falls in the middle, as it should; and beware of blood loss which happens often, and if it occurs, staunch it with that which staunches blood, and care for the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	 from the pustules of the rod
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Often these albathes come to the rod, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; some are malignant and others not; thus you must take them with a subtle lancet, and cut and clean all of them, then place on cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then heal with definite ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul color and stinking, then you must apply cautery there.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 And when you have cut it out, and if the ulcer is partly within the flesh and partly outside, then first remove the part that is inside; and when it is healed, treat the part that is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you treat it together, the ulcer is not assured not to be perforated, and there comes darkness and corruption in its flesh and bone; thus one must cut away all that is dark and corrupted, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from oak bark and lentils, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery helps in two conditions together: that is to say, for bleeding and for corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you insert a leaden tube into the urethra, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hair at the tip of the penis occurs in those who have not been circumcised, due to wound or abscess, it is then necessary that you shave it with one instrument until the foreskin is released, and the head of the penis is freed on all sides; and if it is difficult to discuss this, it is necessary that you shave some of the skin at the tip of the penis and the glans; then carefully separate between two, and place a thin linen cloth moistened in cold water there, so that it does not adhere again.
de la circoncision	 of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 Circumcision is not the separation of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work by our own will, especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best and lightest work for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	 I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they do not practice it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	 For I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around Idal (or Idel), at the strong parts, and on the whole foreskin; so that the heart flees because there are two layers, and perhaps one cuts the upper layer and the lower one remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	 Or the patient recovers slowly, and the pain is double; and in the amputation where the nail is not removed securely, the point of the member may remain; and in the amputation of the fingertip sometimes the iron slips, and it ruins the work, and many times such cases arise that they do not need amputation and I wish it so.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	 Of the amputation done with silken thread I have found the advantage of the experiment, for the silk cuts just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you press your hand and cut evenly in all directions, just ensure the thread is well tightened around the skin; and the manner of the first operation is such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the penis, and then comfort him in every way possible; then hold the penis straight between your hands, and pass the thread between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see it, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the penis and blow into the urethra, and pull up until the glans is inside; then clean well the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the place tightly with a double thread, then tie another thread below the first one; and hold by the second knot with the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two threads, then quickly raise the hand above and pull out the head of the penis; then let the blood flow little by little, for it is the remedy; and put powder on top and on top of the powder a cloth soaked in a mixture of rose water, egg yolk and fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and continue with other treatments until he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 The form of the strength for healing is this: the two hands should be empty and sharp, and the hands should be as large as the wrists equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	 The error in healing is when the heart flows to the incision; therefore, you must stretch it with your fingernail before the place creates an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with pincers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	 And if it passes through three days, and that which is beneath the penis is swollen, then leave it until the abscess has subsided, and gently scrape off the scab; then cut as much as you can move, and beware of the part of the penis, for this will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Cure the place of a sudden wound with powder, as we have said in the treatment of powders, and if it is cut beyond measure and it goes to the heart, it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	 Concerning the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to the concretion of stones, or frozen blood, or bone, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone that is in the neck of the bladder, then the patient must be kneeling on his knees; and his feet must be placed on his back, and he must extend his belly from the top towards the back, and the patient must restrain his anus as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument that is called a "syringe," which has this form: and let it be of fine, light silver, like the feather of a bird; and let the tube be one and a half palms long, and let it be fine at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of releasing the urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie at its end a bag of wool or cotton, and insert the end of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the excess wool and insert it up to the tip of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a chair, and wash the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis back towards the scrotum; then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and the patient will feel it coming to an empty space, and this is not done except according to this order because the conduit in which it goes is twisted; then draw the thread with all the wool bag by bag, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out, and let the urine flow; and restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	 Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	 When scraping or blood enters the bladder, and putrefaction is gathered there, and you pour in water and medicines, then make for all the instrument that is called "clepsydra," and it is like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and let the place where the medicine passes be such that it stops the tube well without addition, so that moisture can be drawn out, and pushed when necessary; and when you pour your medicines into the bladder, put the end of the funnel in the moisture, and draw on the tube that is inside; thus you will draw the moisture into the funnel, and then strongly push the tube back in; thus the moisture will enter, and it will come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder: here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and below at the chest where the band falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in which you want to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a double silk thread, and heat the pouch of that moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the tube, then press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered the bladder; and if you don't have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then insert a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle like an almond, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	 of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	 We have already mentioned in the division the types of stones, and their extraction along with medicines; and I have mentioned the difference between stones in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which stone one should operate to cut; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	 I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder often happens to children, and it is a sign that the urine from the bladder is like subtle water; and there is bloody discharge, and it presses on the patient's penis, and he urinates frequently, and then it stops; and with many of these urinations the foundation [of health] is lost; and it is easy to heal children until they are four years old, and it is very grave in adults, and it is in the middle way for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to purify the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 Because sometimes it hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and lay him flat on his back, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes rises from its place; then have him sit between your hands prepared, and let his hands be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards; then seek and touch inside it; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall with the touch alone, then moisten your finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adolescent; and insert it into his anus, and seek the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, guide it to the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger, and push it out where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 And instruct the assistant to press the bladder in his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the testicles in the area where one makes the cut; then he introduces the cautery instrument, this being its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And make an incision between the area that is between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the vein; and let it be straight upon the stone, and your two fingers should always be on the anus, and let the cut go across so that it is wide outside, and narrow within, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure on the finger in the anus will cause it to jump out without effort; and know that there are such stones which have angles and edges: they are eager to come out; and there are those which are below, similar to a bean, and round, from which the issue is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 At those with angles and edges, make the cut larger; and if it does not jump out, then you must extract it using tweezers that are like a file at the tip, to firmly extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you push underneath the instrument subtly curved at the tip; and if you cannot deceive it thus, then widen the hole somewhat, and if the flesh tears, tighten it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first push the largest into the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull strongly, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, you must saw it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 Because two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes out constantly through the place where the wound cannot heal; but nonetheless you should strive to draw it out, either by pulling or tearing with pincers, until you pull it out piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, then fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it in place, and put on top a cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then lay the patient back on his pillow, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you untie it, wash the area well with oil and water, then treat it with diachylon ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if an abscess or corrosion forms in the wound, and congealed blood in the bladder retains the urine, which is known to pass with the urine: then insert your finger into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, the bladder will become corrupted; afterwards, wash the wound with water and vinegar and oil, and assist him in all ways you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that every time you treat him, you bind his two thighs together, and apply medicines to the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small and it is in the passage of the bladder, and embedded within, and urine cannot pass; then cure him as I have said before, that you cut into him many times, and he will be relieved from the cutting through this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proven it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	 Take a piece of iron according to this shape, and let there be three pointed ends on one stick:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a thread and tie it around the stick under the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then gently push the punch into the stick until it reaches the stone; and turn the punch in your hand against the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce through to the other side of the stone; then urine will come out immediately, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the stick.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is then immediately broken and exits with the urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie one thread under the stone and another on top, then split the stick where the stone is between the two threads, then pull it out strongly, and untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and continue the treatment until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	 of the women’s stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 It often happens that women may have a stone, and if it occurs, the cure is difficult, and is prevented by three things: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled woman who reveals herself to the physicians, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of the hand; and the fourth manner is that the women's stone is more buried than the man’s stone, which requires making a deeper incision, and there is great fear involved. And if necessity compels, it is necessary for you to take a skilled midwife, and one is hardly found, and if you cannot find one, then seek a subtle castrated physician; and present her with a wise maiden in the ways of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command that she do what you command her about the examination of the stone; and watch very carefully if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the anus and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she must press it under her finger, and she should recommend that she insert her left hand into the vagina of the patient, and search and press her left hand strongly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, she must move it from the entrance of the bladder downwards until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike against the stone in the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the anus, where it is most prepared to move, and she will feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the cut be small at first; then push the thread into the cut, if you feel the stone, tighten the wound so that the stone may come out forcefully, and know that there are many kinds of stones: that is to say, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and some have points.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 If you know the signs, you can recognize the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the blood overpowers you, then put ground vitriol on the spot and hold it there for an hour until the blood is stanched; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the instruments I told you about for extracting stones from people to help you in your work; and if the blood overpowers you and it is from the artery that has been cut, then put the powder on the spot and bind it with linen cloths and bandages, and do not attempt this again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, for fear that the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	 And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the place is pale, return to your work until the stone comes out.
de hernie carnouse	 of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	 A watery hernia is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white sack, which is under the heart of the testicles, containing the egg; and it is called "sack", and sometimes it is properly in the skin of the egg, so that one believes it to be another egg; and this is the scrotum of the testicle between the white sack that we have said; and these do not occur unless there is a pouch.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	 And the origin of this hernia is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and that substance is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes it comes from striking the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: either it is inclined towards yellow, or it is redless, or black, or watery white, and this happens often; and these are the signs to recognize this collection, because if it is in the white sack that we have said, then the abscess is reasonable, a long pouch like the shape of an egg, and the testicle does not open, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscess swells with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the thighs and the white silk, one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, prove all the intromissary square, from which the form is as follows.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	 According to what comes after the intromissory, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we cure it with fire, it is necessary that the patient be bled according to his power and the fullness of his body; then have him lie on his back, on something a little high, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod along one of the two ribs at the knee of the thighs; then take the spatula lance, and cut the skin of the thighs lengthwise from top to bottom until near the joint, and let your incision be straight in dividing the skin of the thighs up to the white silk, and delicately peel according to your ability; then pierce the silk thoroughly with water at a wide hole, and drain all the water, and then put your thumb, and stretch the silk up; and do not touch the knee of the thighs, but only the silk; cut or in pieces likewise the side of him delicately, that if you do not cut well wisely, the water will return; and if the egg jumps strongly against your work, then put it back in its place when you have completed the work of the silk; then join the two lips of the knee of the thighs with a suture, then cure as the other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	 And if you find the egg corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you bind the vessels that are suspended, suspecting the flow of blood; then cut the anus completely around the suspended part, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if the egg is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two ramifications; then cut the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put on the wound linen moistened in rose oil; and put outside another linen moistened in wine and oil, and put on the two anuses, and put on doubled cloths, and bind it all with the ligature according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two bandages, and fill them with woolen shreds according to this description, and let them be sewn together at the waist of the breeches; and one of the heads should go underneath from the fundament up to the back, and the other at the wrist; and the other two heads on the two ankles, and let all the bindings be gathered in the loop of the breech; and sometimes this bandage is cauterized instead of iron tailoring, and it is that you take a subtle surgical cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white surface containing the water is revealed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that surface at the ankles, and peel it with this hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And strike in every way that you can, until you have struck everything out; and take care that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more beneficial; and watch for bloodletting, and wounds caused by surgery; and if anything goes against you, whether an abscess or bloodletting or something else, then cure what goes against you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to undergo this procedure because of its dreadfulness, then use perforation, as I tell you; and it is that when you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that pus is present, make the patient sit on a stool; then pierce the abscess in the lower part, making the opening as wide as possible; and make the hole long through the body; and let the hole be wide so that all the water runs out; then place cotton on the spot, and bind it, and let the remaining water drain out, then cure until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to come out of the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a quill or the instrument used to draw water from dropsy patients, as its shape has been described before; and enlarge the hole in the wound, and know that the water will return and be collected again after six months or thereabouts, and when it is collected as before, then the patient will pass his days thus.
de l’aposteme des coions	 Of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the cutting of this vein there is fear in many conditions, which is why I think it is better to leave it alone; and I will tell you the work and similar things about the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	 I say therefore that many abscesses come in the body, especially in the testicles; and this is due to many reasons.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 That is to say, due to excessive bitter and acute humors that are spread in the testicles, or from blows; and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the body; and it does not cause pain, but the abscess is serious; and sometimes there are painful and hard abscesses, with red color, and sometimes they come from a nodule in the artery, or from the swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 Quant il ad vne plaie en la teste, si covient qu'il li soiet mis sus le chief un pan de lin ou une peil de sedes.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 Et cil qui ne puet pas muevre ses genols, si covient que tu metes ung gastel de poyvre vigne a la teste deles les oreilles, ou une gastele de fien enfllee a chauld ewe, ou ung gastele de lin trempet sus la plaie, et c’est bien fait.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 Et se il ad ueines a lor costez, si covient que tu metes les chars suz ces vueines, car ele n’ont mie tant de fors come le uef.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	 And if the base of the flesh is in the posterior place, then you must cut all of it and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when your work is completed, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a bud, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient becomes seriously ill when walking; and the treatment of this disease is almost as dangerous as the previous one, nevertheless we will tell you the work on it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then you pour down the suspensory ligament of the scrotum towards your thighs, over all the vessels near the penis, and the master holds them and stretches them greatly; then cut with a sharp spatula wide from across the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scratch from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in temples; then you insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein comes out, and tie again to the other end; then cut them straight in the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted humors; then treat the wound as with others when a bow is inserted, so that some vessels bleed which nourish one of the testicles; for by this there is no harm, and if at all the vessels come out, it is necessary to pull the testicles at all the vessels; so that the bird does not lose its feeding because of the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	 de la dislocation of the shoulder
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The occurrences of this dislocation are by the section that comes to the shoulder, or the extension on the belly in the area of the intestines, for which the intestines descend from that dislocation into one of the testicles; and this dislocation is either in the shoulder or from the extension of it, and these two types come from many causes: from a blow, from jumping, from leaping, from lifting heavy weights, and from similar things; and the sign when it is from the extension of the shoulder is that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscess is equal all the way to the bottom, because the shoulder presses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	 And the sign is when it is from the section of the sinus, that it brings at the beginning a sudden pain, and the abscess appears diverse, under the skin nearby, and this is due to the exit of the intestines and the body outside of the sinus.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	 And sometimes the coils go with the intestines and are retained therein, causing the patient to suffer great pain, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	 And in these treatments with iron, due to fear, for which it must be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the manner of this operation is that you instruct the patient to reposition the intestine with his hand inside the wound, if he can reach it; then have him sit up on his knees between your hands, and raise his thighs;
