then press down on the abdomen above, and cut all the skin along the length of the testicles; then insert the hooks of the tailor's shears into the groin as many as you need to open the wound, and let it be so wide that the intestines can pass through; then peel off the sinus that is under the skin of the testicles, until the hard white sinus is uncovered on all sides; then insert your index finger in the place where the testicle follows, between the white sinus that is under the skin of the scrotum, and between the second sinus, and separate what is behind the scrotum, and between the second sinus; and then move it with your right hand inside the groin of the testicles, and raise the white sinus high to your left hand, and lift the scrotum along with all the sinuses towards the abdomen; and instruct the assistant to raise the scrotum upwards, and release what is attached behind the ligature; and see with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped in the hard white sinus, and if you find anything, push it down into the abdomen; then take a needle where there are I thick thread made of X threads, and insert it into the back part of the sinus, which is after the skin of the testicles; after the abdomen, then cut the threads that appear from the threads, until there are IVI threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the sinus, which we have said is under the skin of the testicles, with a strong ligature of II parts; then wrap the threads of the threads, and bind them firmly with II parts, so that none of the small vessels that nourish them can enter into it, lest an abscess come there; and put again the ligature according to the first long ligature, and after these II ligatures leave the sinus that is under the groin of the testicles the width of a finger; and after all the other according to the roundness that the scrotum carries; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the testicles, until the blood flows, as we have said before; then bring moistened wool in oil, and place it in the wounds, and bring there the ligature which we have spoken of.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	 And sometimes the white flesh is cauterized after incision, for fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For this happens often, and let the ligament hang by itself; and if it delays in falling out, it should be softened with hot water, and place on it what we have said, until it falls out; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	 of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	 In this case, I have never seen anyone who dared to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is done like the hernia that is together with the bladder, in such a manner that you tie the vessels after slightly cutting underneath; then cut in half, and treat the abscess as one should, until the vessels fall out; and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed. />
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 When an ulcer occurs in the anus, as we have said, it opens up the place; and no one should move any of the intestines to the side, and if they do move, it is little, and they return every hour; but if it stays too long in this state, the ulcer or fistula grows so that the intestines move; and this happens due to the extension of the fistula which is in the anus, as we have said, because it is extended, then the place becomes softened and swollen and open; and the cure for this is cautery, as we have previously said; sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies face up on his back between your hands, then cut the inflamed place of the ulcer wide according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the fistula which is under the skin like a worm, then take the thread and put it on the apparent place of the fistula; and press it deeply into the abdomen, then sew the two apparent places of the fistula on the head of the thread, and sew one and the other; then remove the head of the thread, and do not cut or extend anything else in the fistula, as I have informed you in the cure of the intestine's fissure; then treat it like a wound treatment.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, cleanse it and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	 The sponge is compressed, and there is no appearance in the suture, and the cautery is placed in this place, and it is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	 of the softening of the leather of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	 Often the leather of the testicles is softened in some men because the testes within are softened and it is evident by the milk that can be seen; and it is necessary that when one wants to treat it, they make the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin on top of the natural skin; then join the two lips together with a stitch, and if you wish, first sew the excess softened skin with three or four strong stitches; then cut between the stitches, and treat it as with other wounds until it is healed, and the threads fall out.
dou chastrement	 The scourging
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 You should know that scourging is forbidden in our law, and therefore I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; it is only necessary for two reasons: one is so that the doctor knows how to respond when asked about it, and knows how to treat it; and the other is because we often need to scourge certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I say therefore that scourging is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the method that we perform by attraction, make the beast sit in hot water until the tendons are softened and relaxed; then take them with your hand until they return to their original position and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 From the castration of animals: you must hold the animal, and press its skin around the testicles with your left hand, then tie the rope, and cut each testicle with one cut, when you have well bled them; and leave some pouch of the scrotum and the subtle part that is above the vessels; and this method of castration is milder than that done by attraction, because at attraction perhaps something remains from the testicles, causing the animal to desire lust; then heal the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	 Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 There are two types of hermaphrodites in men: one is when between the two testicles there appears like the female figure of nature, with hair, and sometimes it passes urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other manner is in women, and it is on the wrist like a rod and two inches.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment for men and women is that you cut the cartilages together, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, of the men whose urine comes out through the skin of the penis, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	 of the tonsils
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 The tonsil is a cartilage joined onto the natural part, so that it is too ugly to look at; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 You should hold the excess of the tonsil in your hand or with tweezers, and cut it slightly; and do not go too deep, so that bleeding does not come out, then treat it like other wounds until it is healed; and there is another cartilage that occurs at the mouth of the womb, and it swells, and perhaps comes out, and it resembles a cow’s teat, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow's disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Si it is necessary that you cut it as we have said for the tent, and treat it until it heals.
de erratique	 of the erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 Erratic is when the woman's nature is not well-known, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to illness that has occurred; or it is caused by bad alignment, or subtle or thick cervix, and is done deep in the womb, or on the sides, or below, or wherever; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps menstruation; and knowledge of this is through the examination of the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the blockage is close to appearing, it will seek its way out through two paths or by means of urine.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 S'il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, and let the woman be on her back, with her legs spread; then stretch the two lips very strongly, so that the subtle syfac is round, and there is an overhang; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and let the woman rest at home each day, so that it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the syfac is hard and thick, then you must cut it with a spoon similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the swelling is of fleshy origin, then suspend it in vinegar and cut it; and have the hemostatic medicines, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together with plenty of egg; then bring a wide lead plate, so that the wound cannot heal; and thus let it be for a long time, and bring a tent of dry linen; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when a skin blemish appears on the stomach, it should be covered in this manner, unless it is an ingrown abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For an ingrown abscess on the stomach, one should not attempt to treat it with fire.
des emorroides	 of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually occur suddenly, and when hemorrhoids are old, they become hard; and we have already spoken about their similarities, and their signs, and I will speak here about those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and hard growths, when they are deep in the stomach and cannot be felt, should not be treated with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those who are at the mouth of the wound, which can be felt, are those who can be healed.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 You must therefore place the woman in a cold house, then set the altelul with tongs, and cut off its roots, then sprinkle powdered medicines that restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then dip her feet against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if bleeding continues, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make one plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if it drains, this is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If not, let him be bled with cupping glasses on the back and on the breasts without cutting; then take linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of hawthorn with old wine, and let him bleed at that place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess subsides, then treat the place with onion until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a sharp head, then you must cover it as I have said above; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	 of abscesses of the breast
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many types of abscesses come in the breast, such as cancer and perforating abscess and herpes and osteomyelitis and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatise about the hot abscess that comes to the stomach, which is not one of those that cause fever; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look at whether the abscess is acute in its beginning, full of heat and fever, and if it turns red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Therefore do not hasten to pierce, but let the matter die down until the pain is relieved; then have the patient sit on a chair, and place two small chairs where he can lean, and support his back and draw together his feet on the outside of the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good ligature; then give him to drink towards the left side, and bring there the instrument by which one works the mouth of the stomach, about which comes afterwards the form; and it is necessary that when you have brought this instrument, that you insert the reed first in order to know the depth of the stomach, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not wound the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the stomach with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is necessary that he put the horn of the instrument above, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess is opened, and it is probed with a soft hand, it must be covered at the head with spatula oil; and when the bag is emptied, you must place in the wound tents moistened in rose oil or dry green oil; and put the tent outside of the wound at the bottom of the bandage, and put outside on the bandage and on the finger clean linen moistened in water where mallows have been cooked; then cure it after two days of ointment similar to this, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the bandage and the wound with a clister of water and honey, and then with water and roots of lily and long aristolochia, well-cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is infected on the head, you must be careful not to burn with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	 of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is first necessary for the midwife to recognize the figure of natural childbirth, and its sign is when you see the woman pushing downwards and desiring to smell the air: then know that the child wishes to come out by force; at this point know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue is under the head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends onto its head, the afterbirth comes out with it, and the mother is purged of her superfluities by good purging; and this which happens otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 Because it sometimes occurs in the feet, and it comes strongly in the body or the head, and the hands, where it comes in the stomach, or in the back, and it is turned by chance onto the neck, and other bad shapes; therefore, it is necessary for the nurse that she be wise and skilled in these things, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	 If the child comes onto its head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a saddle where women hold her; and bring up her nature with oil or cooked fenugreek, and then the nurse puts the small spatula between her teeth whose form is thus:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And split the secondine, and cut to its fingernail length so that the moisture inside flows out; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman a clister of fenugreek with sesame oil; then have her take and sneeze condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out strongly, then you must reset them gently little by little; and if they cannot go back in, have the woman sit on a stool and lift her feet up; then knock the stool to the ground, and hold the woman so she does not jump during the fall; and if the hands cannot go back in and the child dies, cut off the hands with the knife mentioned earlier, extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 Of the child's birth onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes onto its feet, it should be pushed upwards; then turn it little by little until it is straightened; then take one foot and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 When he jumps up to his hips, then she should take him and make him sneeze condiments; if he jumps further, so be it with God’s will.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	 And if he does not jump farther as we have said, then turn him little by little until he is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	 For then he will be lightened.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if he does not come farther as we have said, then take a mixture of aloe, and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind all together in a mortar; and apply this ointment on the woman’s genitals both inside and outside; then make her sit in hot water up to her navel; and when she is well soaked below, give her a drink of honey wine, and make her lie down, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on a stool, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose closed, and gently press her belly, for the child will jump now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	 Of the child's birth on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this manner, then put the midwife her hands little by little; then be supported on its neck, and let the feet hang down, and lie on the bed; and bend its hands little by little, and then take the hands above the belly, and remove the pillows from below, until it is ready to pass; and if the child does not come out, then take its feet and move them strongly, then move the belly upwards, then put your hands in; and draw the child little by little; and instruct the woman to push until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	 Of the birth of a child that comes with one hand hanging
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to manipulate the hand: if it cannot be returned, then have the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, then have her lie on a bed and spread her legs wide; then bring in the midwife whom I have mentioned; and if the child does not emerge, then have her sit on a chair, then study how to return the hand; and take the child according to its natural shape, and make it sneeze, and command that she takes hold of herself until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	 from the emergence of the child onto its neck, and its hands spread wide, and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the midwife should take hold of her hand, then turn it little by little, and gently remove it; and when it is equal, place on top the natural midwife of height and oil, as we have said, then command that she move little by little; and when you have done this, have her sit on a chair, and command her to take hold of herself; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	 of this same manner to all the second one
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When it happens in this manner to all the second one, strike the second one with your fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child comes up on its face and on its neck, then cut it from below, so that it is not retained, and let the child die; then push the child back inside, as much as you need to, and instruct the woman to take some time: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	 of the delivery of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	 Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not at all a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two are a strange thing, and do not live, except rarely; I know that they are divided, and are separated by the sinew which divides them, which is tied to the navel; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one all alone, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they come out violently, treat them as we have said, and let the bandage be subtle, and make it quickly and lightly as she does; and do so that it can move for healing.
de plusors enfans	 of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb, one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, and sometimes even more, up to fifteen, all formed in the shape of a child by the skillful measurement of the wise and glorious One, and it is necessary that the bandage know all these things, for similar things may happen; therefore do according to what is needed.
de l’enfant mort	 of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you treat the woman for the dead child in the womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to work by hand, it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and does not have an accident or fear of death; it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, with her head inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the midwife holds two parts, where she is tied to the bed so that she may not be disturbed by the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with althea and fenugreek and flax seed, then anoint the hands of the midwife with these oils and these mixtures; then gently insert them into the womb, looking for one place where they may be convenient for this purpose, and take care if the child is ready to descend onto its head; then place the thorns in his eyes or neck or mouth or soft palate or under the beard or on the forehead or near the ribs, and if the descent is on the feet, place them in the heel and on the middle of the ribs; it is necessary that she hold the thorn with her right hand, and put the pliers between her left thumb and forefinger, and insert her entire hand gently, and place the thorn in any of these places that we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty space; and this is the shape of the thorn:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then insert against the other bone, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then keep them equally steady while moving from side to side, to come out smoothly, and let the bones be sharp-edged to hold well, as shown in this figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if a part remains, smear one of the patient's fingers with oil and press it into that part, and draw out the other part; and if nothing remains, place this bone higher up and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be pulled back due to constriction, it must be wrapped in a cloth until it all comes out; then cut at the joint of the foot or the knee, and you must do the same with the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and it is narrow in the outlet, or if there is sharp water collected at the top, then you must insert the pointed spatula between your teeth, and make an incision in the head and extract the water; or pass it to the instrument that is called "almidach," from which the form comes with the instruments in the following chapter; and do likewise if the child has a large natural head; then draw out the bones with forceps, and if the head comes out and it is stuck at the pelvis, then split it until the water that is in the bladder comes out; and if it cannot come out, then strike it into pieces with the hammer as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the water runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	 And if the child is on its feet, then the attraction is light, and the reception at the mouth of the mother is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is stuck in the belly or the breast, you must extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and make an incision in the belly or the breast, until the moisture inside comes out; and if the other limbs are removed and the head remains, then the nurse places her hand deep into the mother's body, and pulls it to the mouth of the womb; then she puts one or two onions there, and pulls strongly; and if the mouth of the womb is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has formed, you should not struggle with it, but rather apply moist and fatty things; and the nurse prepares poultices and applies a softening and moistening decoction.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the child is on its side, and you can set it straight, then treat it as we have said for a living child; and if you cannot do so, then draw out the limb piece by piece, leaving nothing of the second joint.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when you have done this, treat it as we have said for abscesses that come in the marrow; and if blood flows out, put it in boiling water to stop the bleeding, and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	 And I saw a woman whose womb an infant had died in, then another came on top of it, and the other also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	 After a long time, an abscess came to her womb, and it swelled so much that it burst open, and she began to suffer greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	 I was called to the treatment, and I thought for a long time, and the wound could not be healed.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	 I applied a strong drawing plaster, and an (first) bone came out, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	 I was greatly amazed, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	 Then I thought that these were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I explored the wound and drew out many bones until the woman was in better health; and she lived for a long time thus, and it always exuded a little pus from that place; and I did not record this chapter except because, when the master finds something strange, he should know how to put help there.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	 To return the wound to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	 Here comes the form of the press, with which one uses the books; and at two turns are the two keys of the two locks.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 Nevertheless, let the horns of the restrictor be more subtle, and made of ebony or boxwood; and let the mouth of the beam be two fingers wide, and the edge of the arbor one finger, and in length a palm and a half; and between the two locks there should be two adjustments of this same beam, which are fixed in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are pushed into the mouth of the wound to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, made more subtly and lightly from ebony or boxwood according to the appearance of tongs; and let there be two adjacencies at the two heads, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the vulva with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging and her legs spread, then push the two adjacencies together into the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; then work your hand along the entire instrument, as you have done with the tongs equally, according to the amount by which you wish to open the mouth of the vulva, so that the vagina does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	 This instrument is all superior, and their resemblances are multiplied; and when the master has prepared them, then the work is all the more urgent, and higher for men by their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	 Do not despair of the instrument until you have prepared it, for their necessity is not negligible.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze vigorously, and press your hands to her mouth and nose; and if she faints from this, it will be well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, then take a pot and make a hole in the lid, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cinnamon, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in the pot with water over the fire; then place a tube or hole from the pot to the mouth of the woman, and hold it until the vapors enter the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	 If the second bone jumps suddenly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment and is not strong, command the maid to moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or muslin cloth with aloe vera, then put it into the vagina, and search for the bone; and when she has found it, take hold of it and pull it out little by little straight, so that the womb does not fall out during extraction; but it must be moved gently to the right and to the left, and then pull; thus it will come out and detach itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 And if the mouth of the womb is tightly constricted, we have spoken of the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not come out from all that we have said, be careful not to force during pulling; but it is necessary that he who is at the mouth of the womb tie it to the thigh of the woman, then administer a clyster of tetrapharmakon enema; thus it will rot and return, and become strong; however, when it rots, bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	 If it is necessary, therefore, for fumigations suitable to this: some of the ancients have proven fumigations with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	 The form of the instrument with which one fumigates a woman to retain her flowers and secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it is of glass similar to a vase, and one puts the subtle end in the nature, and the wide ends on the fire; and let the fumigation be over coals, and continue until the tinea is completely eradicated, and then begin another.
de percier lou fondement	 of piercing the anus
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born with their anus not pierced, but rather stopped by a thin membrane: it is therefore necessary for the midwife to pierce that membrane with her finger, and not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and take care that she does not touch it; then apply a linen cloth moistened in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	 And if you doubt that it will not heal, put a plug of lead in the hole, and leave it there for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	 And sometimes this happens suddenly from a wound or abscess; then you must cover that sudden swelling: and it should be treated as we have said with the plug of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	 of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from below the anus are nodules, and those that come beside the anus are outside, or in the space of the two parts, sometimes there is one fistula or several; and when this nodule is old, it works, and increases moisture, a foul-smelling pus, either white or subtle, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are known by the fact that there is discharge or gas during defecation, and perhaps some are painful.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	 And so for fissures that reach as far as the bladder, and to half of the penis; and they extend as far as the hip joint, and to the end of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one recognizes the fissure piercing through the anus, and not piercing: it is that you insert your index finger into the anus, and insert a fine needle of bronze or iron into the fissure when there is no convolution.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 And if there is convolution, then insert a thin probe of lead, or a horsehair, until you feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and nothing comes out of the opening except air, know that it does not pierce through; thus hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	 And when the fistula extends to the bladder or to the urinary tract, then the urine leaks out, and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is perforated to the junction of the thigh, then the tent is coming to that place; if there is no tortuosity and the location of the pain around it, then it is that it exits always bowed, and neither ointment nor medicine by cautery helps; and in these penetrating fistulas there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In that which is not penetrating and is not ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proven, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and raise his legs up to his thighs, and let his thighs be inclined towards his belly; then insert a tent of tin, or lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your finger there, and if you feel that the tent is perforated; and if it is uncovered where you feel between your finger the sphincter or the flesh, then know that it is perforated; do not work on it anymore as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 However, it is said that some can be healed well, but this happens rarely; and the aid that one provides there, is to heat the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as was previously stated; and insert it all hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the anus; and do this two or three times, so that you know that those charred hairs are burnt, which are like a feather of a bird; and then cure the moist tent with butter, so that that hair comes out, then cure the inflammation with ointment, healing flesh and sinew.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If he is thus healed, this is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If it is not otherwise possible to be healed in this manner; and if the tent enters, but does not perforate up to the finger that is at the base, and there is a thick covering of flesh or silk between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula at that which follows the covering of the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the tent forward continuously, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the top of the tent; and the tent will be delivered and fall; then clean those fleshy parts that resemble a bird's feather, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	 And if the pus overcomes you, and flows between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 Car the fire cautery accomplishes two good things: namely, the burning of these hairs adjacent to one another, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then the treatment of wet tents in butter or in ground substances, until the place gives off steam, and thus the burned hairs are in the steam; then treat the wound with pastes made from hard-healing plants, which are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	 Car when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	 And if the fistula goes all the way to the bottom of the anus and is separated from the body, place your finger in the anus and search for it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 And if you feel the tent and there are two things inside it, either cloth or silk or hair, which is close to piercing through, do not leave until you see a path of confidence and hope, by administering one of the three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it all the way to the bottom, or if you can place tents and treat as before; and do not go too deep that you do not cut the support which holds the anus, and the evacuation goes out without control; then treat as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or remove that covering and clean it after it is cut near the anus, either by tent or by another pointed instrument; then clean that faulty hair that is in the wound, as much as you can; then strive to restore the wound and keep the fistula in the part outside the anus: this will be a lighter burden for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fistulas are in this manner: and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is at the side of the foundation near the skin above, then take a pierced tent at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	 And in it you put a twisted thread in two, and push the tent along the entire thread into the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is protruding from the edge of the foundation within, then extract the thread from that opening, so that you push your finger into the foundation; and pull the head of the thread, and join the two heads together, and press one against the other, and leave it for a day or two; and bind it sometimes, until the thread cuts these vessels that are between them, and they bleed; then treat the wound until it is healed and healthy. ię If it is protruding from the edge of the foundation within, then extract the thread from that opening, so that you push your finger into the foundation; and pull the head of the thread, and join the two heads together, and press one against the other, and leave it for a day or two; and bind it sometimes, until the thread cuts these vessels that are between them, and they bleed; then treat the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	 If the fistula does not open, then have it pierced in all ways that you can, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For it is not appropriate to cover the opening so deeply for the healing, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The form of the sharp spine used to make the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	 from hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there may be small or large ones, and there is always a little blood near them, and there may be one or several, and they are outside the anus and at the edge of the anus; but those that are outside have less moisture, and always a little yellowish water or a little blood, and have the color of the flesh; and the cure for those who have them inside the anus is to instruct the patient to squeeze to go to the latrine until the anus protrudes and the threads appear; then hasten, and hold it with tweezers, or with your fingernail, then cut at its roots; and if the fingernails cannot hold them because of their moisture, take them with a cloth or with cotton, or with a piece of flannel; and draw them to your teeth, then cut them, and sprinkle some hot powders that should be in place of cautery; or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure with other cures until healed; and if the anus cannot protrude, then enema the patient with a biting and harsh enema to clean what is in the anus so that it can come out openly; when the patient squeezes, and the threads are out of the anus, the cure is light; and it is to take them with your fingernail or with tweezers, and cut them, then cure as we have said until healed, and to avoid cutting with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, and then draw the thread through on top and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread underneath the needle, making it wide; and then tighten the thread strongly, then knot the thread, and pull out the needle, and do this for all the others, leaving one to drain any excess blood; then place on top a cloth soaked in rose oil or wax, and place on top, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until it festers, and when they have fallen, cure them with ointment and other care until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	 when of dryness of the fire or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	 Often occurs dryness of the fire in the intestines, and by natural constraint, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then you must burn with the point of a spatula or your fingernail the skin above it so that it does not moisten; then treat it until it is dry as needed; and if it cannot be dried, then start the scraping again more strongly than before, until it bleeds profusely and is scabbed; then treat it until it heals.
dou fremit	 from trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 Ants are small creatures that inhabit the body and penetrate very deeply; sometimes cold finds them, and they feel it just like a trembling death, and it spreads throughout the entire body, more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the treatment is such that you take a reed from a goose feather, or a strong feather from an ox, and place that reed on the tremor, until the ring grasps the tremor all around; then turn your hand with the entire reed until you cover the entire tremor, and put it inside deeply, and pull out the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	 And if you see this, then do so with a reed of bronze or iron according to this form, and let it be thin below and sharp above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	 nor should it be pierced to hold on the finger, and press more And if you see this, then cauterize the tremor as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	 of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	 Sometimes one makes an enema of silver or copper, or melted iron or brass; and sometimes one makes them from these instruments small and large, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	 Therefore, those which are prepared for the treatment of children who are weak and sickly are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	 The form of the small and large enema is thus wide, where the stomach is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 and there must be an opening where the stomach is tied, as you see, and the end is pierced; and on one side there are two openings, and on the other one; and the stomach in which the medicines are placed should be of a beast’s bladder or parchment, and should be pierced all around with small openings, and there should be one fingerbreadth between each opening. Then insert into these openings a strong thread made of twisted wool, making an X or a circle around it; and tie the stomach like this as if it were a goatskin; and when the medicine is inside, then bind it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the enema; and that is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg yolk, or similar substance, then insert it gently; then the servant expresses it with his two hands together, until it is all void, then remove the clyster, and have the patient raise his legs against the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, then hold it as much as possible; and if he sleeps a full night, then it is of greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you administer the clyster in an illness of a distended abdomen, and the medicine hastens to exit, then repeat it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if there are hemorrhoids or an abscess in the rectum, let the clyster be as thin as for a child; and this is the form of a thin clyster on which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	 of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	 We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicines according to their uses.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	 I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are by the fall of a stone, and by the cut of a sword or knife, or by a spear or club or arrow, or by similar things; or they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or on the foot, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, because their treatment will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from the impact of a stone or similar things, and the skin is nevertheless torn and the wound is large, and you suspect hot abscess: then quickly cauterize with cephalic immediately if there is little blood from the wound, and let the cautery be on the opposite side of the injured part; and make sure the patient avoids overindulgence in wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he does not want to cauterize, let his food be reduced, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come there, only cotton moistened in rose oil or stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and not moved by air, powder that I will tell you a little later; and if the ars has moved it, put some ointments until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.
