And if the wound is large such as from a sword cut and similar, and the lips of the wound cannot be brought together by tension, then sew them together, as I will say for wounds of the belly, with stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is open to the bone and gaping, and holds together only at one point, then cut away that point; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as cheeses and cooked grain, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find rot in the skin that reaches to the bone, then cut away all the rotten flesh and cast it aside, then treat [the wound]; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein from which blood flows that cannot be stopped by medicines, then seek out the artery, and if you find it dislocated, bind it with a thread; and if this does not help at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	 And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: and it is that you put in this powder which heals before the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and make it into a fine powder, and fill the wound, and press it firmly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it unbound if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	 And sometimes one does this only with quicklime, when one has no frankincense or dragon's blood, but that the fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the fire has moved the wound, even in summer, do not put this powder on it; but put some cooked onions on it, or poultices made of barley flour with water and honey, until it flows out; then continue other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you later about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	 of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	 If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 Si c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, and cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, and autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, and oignemens moistes.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound is large, sew it shut and bind with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and it is cut and full of bile, then pierce it in a lower place; and if the artery is cut, and blood comes out, then suture it, and bind it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the conduit is protected, so that the flesh goes, then sew the heart onto the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then bind it firmly, and leave it for some days, then cure it with dry onions until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then search for it; and if there are pieces of bone, then draw them all out if you can, and those that you cannot have, then leave them until the wound rots, and is emptied and cleared of the issue; and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle with powder onto the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	 And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	 Of the lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 And if it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, observe if there is any foul odor coming from the patient: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at the first hour, nor bind it tightly so that the blood does not escape deeply and returns to the heart, and kills the patient; but apply atractive ointment and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb excess moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; so that spasm, tremor of the heart, or strangulation will not occur; and when you see favorable signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Cure it with dressings and other treatments until he is healed; and if it cannot heal, and there is pus, then know that there is a fistula; treat it as necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut and it is simple, either worse or on the back, then treat it with that which is in front; if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is close to the bone and has struck pieces, then seek the wound, and remove the splinters if they are loose; and if they are not loose, then let the wound fester, which will lighten the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	 Of the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The rupture of the abdomen is great, medium, and small; in a large wound, sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out, because of which the reinsertion of them becomes difficult; and often a small wound is worse than a large one, because it is more difficult to reinsert the intestines if they are not put back in immediately, for the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, and thus enter more difficultly. And therefore, a medium-sized wound is better, because it is easier to return the intestine to its place than in others II Know that the sutures of the abdomen are according to four kinds: the two common stitches occur during the stitching of the abdomen, and the stitches of other wounds of the body and two other stitches are common to other wounds; however, they are more specific with the stitching of the abdomen, and I will speak about each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestines has come out, and it is a great thing to put back, this is done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten one sponge or cloth in lukewarm water only, or boil cinnamon and cypress and cloves in wine, and bathe the intestine until the swelling is gone; sometimes this restraining wine is necessary, and it is better to use alone for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling diminish, moisten the intestine in water where althea and mallow have been boiled, for by this means the entrance is made easier a little; and if it cannot enter, make an opening in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is better than cutting, no one should cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument to split: cut inside the curve and not outside, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is opened and the intestines jump out, place them back according to their natural form in their proper place, if you have the power, for this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, you must make the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the upper part of the belly, place the head and the breasts higher than the lower parts, and likewise if the opening of the belly is in one of the two parts, direct your attention so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus you must administer as I say in large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, use what you have prepared, then take in your hands a careful minister who can dye the entire edge with his hand, and bring together the lips; this is the common method of sutures, and it is that you take one needle or several, according to the width of the wound, then leave two fingers' worth of space from the head of the wound, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread; pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the hypodermis, which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierce on that side, and bring together the two heads of the hypodermis along with four together; then draw a double thread around the needle on both sides, then bring together the two heads of the wound in the same way, and then leave two fingers' worth of space, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need from the needles, until the entire wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium-sized, between subtle and thick, for subtle needles pierce all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well: therefore they must be medium-sized; and it is not necessary to push the needles too far from the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and work the wound before the suture; and then cut the heads of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put bandages or cloths on the heads of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; this method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because an additional needle is sufficient in a second suture, which is common, and it is that you bring together the two heads of the skin and the two heads of the hypodermis together at one needle where there is a good medium-sized thread; and when you have pierced these four heads together, then remove the needle to the part where you began, in the manner in which one sews clothes; and put space between each suture equal to the thickness of a small finger; this suture holds well, and I sewed a wound that a man had on his stomach, which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm in size, and two palms of intestines came out, and the wound was in the middle of the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 Je lui remis les intestins après qu'ils eurent été hors pendant vingt-quatre heures, puis la blessure fut scellée jusqu'à quinze jours, et je l'ai soigné, et il a guéri.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I put on the wound old cotton II times a day, and I washed it with honey water until he was cured.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Now I will tell you the II proper ways of stitching: take the needle and pass it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced the heart straight through, leave the tip of the thread where you passed the needle, and make it come out on the other side from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew like the furrier makes the furs, and that you leave one time the thread on one side, and take it back on the other, until the stitching is all done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 Li seconde maniere de costure, that is the second manner of stitching, which Galen mentions specifically, is done as follows: some people bring together the two parts naturally, and apply one end of the silk to the other end, in this manner: insert a needle at the end of the thread close by, and have it pierce only that place, and leave the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part until it reaches inside, at the two ends of the silk; then make both ends from the outer part reach inside, in two other places of the thread which are on either side; and this is the second manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens says this word, and some attest to it: one should suture the belly with two needles, each with thread; and one must insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew straps; and know that when the incision is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the fire has moved it, then you must cauterize the intestine and the wound; then apply a powder enchanting flesh, and if the fire has moved it, then apply some ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and sew the threads, and let the siphac and mirach be soldered; then treat the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then apply, as soon as it begins to cast pus, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 Car you do not need other medicine in many situations when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will spread to the main members, then it is necessary that you moisten a light cloth in oil of tempered heat, or in rose oil, and place it around the joints and under the armpits; and if there is pain or corruption in the bowels, which often happens, then give clysters of tepid black wine, and likewise if the corruption reaches the intestines; and pierce within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine that is called "jeune" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is due to the thinness of the veins present there, and due to the subtlety of the whole body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the intestine protrudes from the wound, replace it like the intestines while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned black or brown, you must tie off the black part so that blood does not flow therein, for there are veins and arteries; then cut between the ties, and hang both ends of the section below the wound until they dry out to ease the extraction when the intestine falls back into place.
de la routure dou boueil	 of the bladder's rupture
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is cut and the wound is small, it can be restored in some cases, for I have seen a man wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and turned into a fistula, from which excrement and gas were emitted; I treated it as best I could and did not cease until he was healed and the place closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it heal, I feared that the patient might have an ailment in his belly; and there was no ailment, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in such a manner: take large-headed pins, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the pin has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips, so that it draws its mouth up; and then strike the head, and this holds so that it cannot come loose, then place another pin afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely enclosed; and stitch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 Those heads thus adhere in the intestines, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestines with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner: take the head of this intestinal thread that is very thin, and then tie it at the end of this thread a fine twisted linen thread, then put the thread through the needle, and sew the intestines, and bring them back together; and this method of suturing for fractures is not beyond according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the hollow intestines, there is neither skill nor health, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	 Of a fistula, wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that any wound or abscess, when it breaks open, is universally called a "fistula," and also when it bursts and exudes pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And a fistula is, in truth, a hard and white scar that does not cause pain, and it also bursts like the quill of a bird; sometimes it exudes clear pus, other times thick; sometimes little, other times enough; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh in it, it is not healed except by one of the NINE causes: that is to say, due to the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh within, on the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine in the treatment is not good; or because the corruption is a manner of plague; or due to the nature of the region, digestion is slow, and healing is delayed, and it is swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	 Or it is necessary that I make you know the cure of fistula which is made by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas which come to the large veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves, or to the liver, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and there are such that come to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all the fistulas which are of this kind are of grave healing, and there is no remedy except labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula which does not come up to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you want to know it, then take a probe of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, then seek it; and if the fistula is crooked, then search for it with a subtle probe of boxwood, because boxwood bends more easily around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well seek it with probes, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for moisture goes from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then wisely seek it according to your ability, so that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and cut deeply into it, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels at the pressure of your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint or a nerve or an artery or a vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the foulness and corrupt flesh that is within; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep from the right place, then it is necessary to cut deeply into it, as much as you can, then put moist probes in medicinal vinegar, and pour them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the superfluity which remains at the bottom; and then put dressing in fresh meat, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupt from the fistula, then cut into it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If a vein or nerve is damaged in the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed and there is decay and blackness, then scrape it until all the decay is removed, then treat with healing flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and bleeds again as before, know that you are not yet at the source: uncover and seek until you reach the source, remove all the decay, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the decay is too deep for you to reach; then there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature; and if there is a little bone decayed, and you can draw it out with pincers, draw it out with an instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, draw them all out, do not leave any; and if moisture hinders you, and there is no error or fear, cut flesh and moisture and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place on the wound something that causes putrefaction, and leave it until the place is rotten around the bones, and then the bones will more easily come out; and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, then remove only the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption, and it reaches to the marrow of the bone; then you must cleanse and scrape all the way to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 He was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg from something that came into the body, causing matter to accumulate in the leg and forming a large abscess which swelled up. There was no reason to open it; but the doctors in their foolishness kept working on it until the abscess burst open, and much matter flowed out. It became an ulcer with many holes that all oozed pus and moisture from the body. Many doctors tried to treat it for two years without any success, until I was called to see him. I saw his leg and the medicines they were using, as well as the large amount of matter flowing from the holes. The young man's skin turned red and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 Je (I) boutai (pitched/set up) une (a) tente (tent) en (in) l’un (one of) ces (these) pertus (holes/passages), et (and) puis (then) cerchai (sought out) toz (all) les (the) pertus (holes/passages), et (and) trovai (found) que (that) li (the) uns (one) venoit (came) encontre (against/towards) l’autre (the other) de (of) toutes (all) les (the) parties (parts/sections) de (of) la (the) jambe (leg).
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 Je me hâtai donc (so I hurried then), et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je découvris une partie de l’os (and dug into one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone), et le trouvai corrompu et percé (and found it rotten and pierced), et venoit la corruption jusqu’à l’os dedans (and the rot extended to the inside of the bone); je nettoyai ce que m’apparaissait de l’os corrompu (I cleaned off what appeared to be the rotten part of the bone), et crus qu’il n’y aurait pas d’autre corruption, sauf celle que j’ôtai (and thought there would be no other rot except for what I removed); et commençai à traiter la plaie avec des remèdes adoucissants pendant longtemps (and began to treat the wound with softening remedies for a long time), mais elle ne put cicatriser (but it could not heal); et puis recommençai (and then I started over again), et redécouvris l’os comme avant (and rediscovered the bone as before), et trouvai la corruption continuée dans l’os (and found that the rot had spread throughout the bone), et la nettoyai (and cleaned it off), puis l’ôtai (then removed it), et me penai de souder le lieu (and worked to heal the place); mais je ne pus tant que je creusai autour d’une palme de l’os (but I could not do so until I dug around a palm's width of the bone), et le traînai hors de tout son moule (and removed it from its whole cavity), puis le traitai avec des remèdes (then treated it with remedies); et il fut sain et soudez rapidement (and it quickly became healthy and healed), et ne fallut plus recommencer l’ouvrage, sauf pour la faiblesse du malade (and there was no need to start over again except for the weakness of the patient), qui ne pouvait supporter (who could not endure it), et pour la peur de la mort que j’avais de lui (and out of fear of his death that I had).
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Because of the evacuation of blood, he often bled profusely, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone, hard flesh grew, and it was well-disposed and had no harm or contrary effect at all, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be set in this manner: take a bandage, and tie it at the end of the open bone, and command someone to extend it upward; and place another bandage of linen thicker than the first bandage, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone, and stretch the top, so that you draw the corrupted flesh downward, and discover the flesh above the place where you want to set [the bone], so that the splint does not harm the flesh; and place a piece of wood or a board under the bone to move the corrupted flesh; and it is necessary to set as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and to set again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is rotten and does not open, and the rotting is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh; then put a glowing ember underneath, and then saw through the rotten part from one side to the other; and let the saw be longer than the rotten part by a thumb’s width, as we have said; and if the rotting is at the joint, then cut off the rotten joint, and saw the bone on the other side where it is not rotten; and if the rotting is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut; and if the rotting is in the palm of the hand or the sole of the foot, this is a very serious matter; nevertheless, you must seek out this rotting, how it opens for you; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but let the vein or nerve not work against you; and know that the instruments for incising these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and delicacy, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare for each similar task its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument of which you have need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the instrument of which you have need according to what is required.
dou feu	 From the fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head may putrefy from within or without; and when you have treated that corruption with the cure of medicines, and they do not benefit, it is necessary to amputate that limb up to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes death or the greater evil of the loss of the limb. The sign of this is that the limb becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and then putrefies after the blackness; thus goes that corruption from limb to limb, and spreads throughout the body. Therefore, hasten to amputate, and if it is from the bite of some venomous animal, such as a sea scorpion or viper, if the corruption is at the fingertip, cut it off and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches the hand, then cut at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cut with a knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and no treatment will help except in proportion to its virtue; and do the same when the corruption comes to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, then cut after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, then cut off the entire foot; and if it goes up the leg, then cut at the knee joint; and if it reaches above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die; and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is such that you tie it above and below, and extend one ligament downward and another upward, and you remove the flesh between the two ligaments to a width of half a finger, until the bone is exposed; then cut or saw, and place on each side a bandage of linen, so that the saw does not touch the healthy place, and thus comes another injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if bleeding occurs while you work, cauterize the place quickly, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: there was a blackness that resembled a burn from fire, and this corrosion first came on his big toe of the foot, so much so that it spread throughout the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover his foot, and it was healed; and a long time after, the corrosion returned to the big toe of the hand, and he came to me, and I put on repellent things after cleansing the body, but the corrosion could not cease; and he asked that I cut off his hand, and I did not want to, for I hoped to drive out the matter; and I also feared that if I cut his hand, he might die, because the man's vitality was weak; and he became completely desperate, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and it was healed; and I have told this story only so that others may learn from it, should they need to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy place and stays so long that it causes a large gathering of pus; then it roars and bursts, and the pus jumps out, leaving the place empty, just like a vessel; and the skin on top is as thin as delicately woven cloth, and does not extend to the bone or nerve. Such an illness is called "health" and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so much that it reaches the bone profoundly, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you can cut all around it, even when it is thin, just like delicately woven cloth; and it does not hurt because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if you trust that the skin has healed, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it with an enema in this way: see if the breast is large, and the discharge from it is of foul odor, then enema with Egyptian medicine made thus: take asafoetida, oil, and lead, equally, and put to cook in a vessel over fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey; and then take some of this according to your need, and mix it in water and honey, and enema the breast, and close the orifice; and leave the medicine inside for II hours, then extract it by pressing; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed; and sometimes enema with ash water, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of vine wood, and pour water over it, then strain it, and enema, until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then enema with water and honey where there is a little lead powder; or enema with honey and mixed wine, that the honey may have the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the wound dry; and when you have done this, and you trust that the breast is well cleansed, then enema with what produces flesh in it, and it is that you take definite plaster, and mix it with rose oil and in wine; or enema with some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have said in the treatise of ointments; and if the orifice of the breast is small, and the tube of the enema cannot enter, then widen it a little with an iron, and insert a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, then sew it up, leaving only one place where the enema can enter, and if the orifice that discharges bowel is at the top, then cut lower or in a lower place.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 Car when the arrow is completely inside, it does not allow flesh to enter; and if you cannot remove the skin as you wish, then prepare in such a manner that the arrow goes to the lowest place where it is, for when the arrow is completely inside, it does not allow flesh to enter; and if you cannot remove the skin as you wish, then prepare so that the arrow goes gently downward, and leave nothing of the arrow; and take medicines that strengthen for placing on the wound, and stretch over a cloth of linen that covers all the wound; then cut strongly at the place of the breast, making the hole wider than before, then stretch a soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the hole, and put it on the hole of the wound to lighten the arrow, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and that which is on the hole of the breast, remove often to remove the arrow, and know what comes out of the arrow, whether it is poison or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not; and when your medicine has been extended in this manner and you see the nature that rises on the hole of the wound, know that the breast is already healed, and health approaches; and then remove it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you open the wound, then change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	 And if the chest throws out undigested food after many days, know that the chest does not breathe.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poisons course through after a long time, do not despair of health, for healing approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 And if wounds heal slowly with the formation of flesh and some do the opposite; and if undigested food is ejected from the chest after many days, know that the chest does not breathe; and if the chest delays in breathing and is distant, then approach with drying medicines that are moist in substance but dry in virtue, as described in the ointment of diafin, for there is a large part of vitriol, which is the final medicine. Take diafin ointment and make it with rose oil and wash it with equal old wine in substance; then infuse and use it; and the same thing cooked and thickened works better when diafin ointment is not present. If you do not have mirrah and aloe and incense, take them and grind them into a powder on honey while it is on the fire; and then glue it with cloth and place it on the chest, and sometimes we administer long aristolochia root and celestial lily root, which are also like vetch flour and centaury. And use either simple or compound: grind them into a powder and mix with the honey I mentioned and use it; and if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption has reached deep, and presses on the bone, or on hard members, or on joints. Then cure the fistula as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	 of the fingertip abscess
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Paronychia is an abscess that forms under the fingernail of the hand or foot, or possibly in other places; and when it becomes old and neglected, there will be a stinking abscess, which runs and throws pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly all the way through; and it eats away at the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the tip of the finger is wide, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you cut off with an iron all the excess that remains from the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy and the flesh is clean; but if the flesh presses into the flesh, begins to prick and wound, then you must place a razor under the nail that pricks the flesh, and push it up, and carefully and lightly cut off that flesh, and apply burning and corrosive medicines on top to remove everything; then treat with ointments until healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and draw strongly, for as long as the corrupt bone is there, it cannot heal; and if you see the toe begin to rot, cut it off at one of our fingers, as mentioned before, then treat until healed; and if it is struck, and swollen, and the patient feels great pain, then you must first stop the bleeding; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula by cutting diagonally on top, and ensure that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	 The pain of the shoulder of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two thumbs that appear in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and sometimes there is one with bones, and sometimes there is a claw. And sometimes they are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 That which is born in any knuckle of the thumb does not move, and that which is born at the joint of the thumb may perhaps move; the shape of the fleshy one is light, in this way: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	 That which is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; so hold yourself ready with the scalpel.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In one who is born or should at the anus, you must first cut the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable saw, then heal it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	 The swelling that comes to both together comes from birth, or from the healing of a wound, or from burning by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 Then you must cut this swelling so that the parts may return to their natural shapes; then place between two tents or cloths moistened with rose oil, so they do not rejoin; or you place between two thin sheets of lead until the place is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	 If swelling comes to one of his hands with the palm, cut this swelling as needed.
des vils	 of the vile
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 Veins are large swollen and full of superfluous melancholic humors that come in many parts of the body; and it happens more in the legs of those who walk, work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	 Therefore, you must administer some purging of bile to him, and then heal it with the balm of Mecca.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment with iron is done in two ways: one is that they are cut and drawn out the black blood; and the other way is that you lift the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The incision is done in this way: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the thick blood becomes thin; then hold the patient's leg from above the hip to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three places, with a wide cut; then lift and draw out the black blood forcefully by hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can bear; and then bind it, and command him to eat foods that generate black bile; and repeat the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and it will benefit the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The elevation of it is as follows: raise the patient's leg, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it turns red, and inflate the veins; and if you don't have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut near the vein from the hip to the knee or in the part below the ankle; then work the skin with scissors, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then push the thread down, so that it is raised from the skin, and then gently pinch it with tweezers, then cut in another place above three fingers; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then raise it with thread as you did before, and pinch it with tweezers as you did first; then make another cut, or several if you need to, then raise it and cut at the toe of the foot, then draw it out and raise it up to the second cut; then pull it from cut to cut, until it comes out completely, then cut it; and if you cannot draw and raise it, put in a needle with one strong double thread, tie it and draw it, put it under a thread, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out; and be careful that it does not cut, because if it cuts, it cannot be drawn or raised, and it harms the patient; and when you have completely drawn it, put moistened wool in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and heal it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is contracted and twisted and wrinkled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it obliquely, but do not chop it; and pull it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The form of the iron used to cut the face is curved and does not cut cleanly, so that it does not cut the vein; and it is thick, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein. But let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is found in the legs, in hot regions where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land; and it may occur elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to the corruption that comes beneath the skin, as snakes and worms enter between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is such that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then the place changes, and the vein begins to come out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the head opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of lead from one and a half to two and a half palms long, including the knot, and leave the lead hanging on the leg; and every time some comes out of the hole, wrap it around the lead and the knot. And if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the rest, but do not cut at its base until it is completely removed; because if you cut it, it will enter into the flesh, and cause an abscess and rotting in that place, and a bad disease; for which reason it must be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein, when it is drawn out five or ten palms long, and there was one man who came to me whose it came out ten palms long, and when you cut it, it spurts a stream or a hole, and pierce until the bottom so that all comes out; and clean out the material that is inside, and apply medicines on the place each day that prevent rotting, then treat it as for abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein there is little blood, especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or leg, and much blood comes out, and then it runs less; treat it then as we have said before.
