Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the break is near the shoulder's head, then you must place one ligament in the middle under the armpit and another towards the back, below the break; and similarly, if the break is towards the back, then you must place one ligament lightly, without force, until the break is level with the joint and the back; then set the break as it should be and hold it, so that a boil does not form there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	 And if such a boil forms there, do not hold it until the seventh day, and place a moist linen cloth with ass's milk and rose oil on it until the boil is appeased; then hold it, and the manner of holding it is that you place the plaster on the break, then bring the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put the bandage on, and hold above the shoulder and the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, unless something prevents it, or unless the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 And if you doubt that the bone will move, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, with two fingers' width between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes beyond the fracture by three fingers on each side; then draw up the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter above the fracture, more strongly and less widely apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the positioning of the splints and the tightening as we have said, at the hour when you restore the broken limb, and you doubt that there is a hot abscess, let it be bound until the seventh day as we have said; then check the bandage every three days to ensure that irritation or swelling does not occur in the place, lest nursing cannot come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If he receives it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such accidents happen, do not untie it before after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach; and place one cushion full of wool under the shoulder, and watch every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not move, nor is the ligament weakened; so receive it by the power of medicine, and give him the food that we mentioned earlier, in such a way that the food is first fine; and when he begins to regain strength, let it be coarse.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be taken for forty days in total; and then one should untie it and administer a bath and ointment medicines to heal the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the stricture is ugly and clogged, then it takes I day or II months to untie.
de la brisure du bras	 of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 The arm is composed of II bones, which are called the two "foscile," one of which is small, and it is the one that follows the wrist; and the other is large, and it is the one that is underneath, towards the little finger; by chance, only the large foscile breaks, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small foscile is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, then the healing is bad, and more serious than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then you should stretch it slightly and set it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large bone that is broken, then you must pull it more strongly; and stretch it on a cushion, and hold the little finger of the hand higher than the others, and the small toe lower than the other toes, and let the patient be cross-legged over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher so that the patient suffers no labor; then the assistant stretches his arm towards the part below his hand, or at the ligament, and another assistant to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 Then let the physician set it straight, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if in the break there are fragments, then place each one in its proper place; and if any are protruding that touch the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut above and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	 And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a particular chapter; take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if in the beginning of the restoration apostemes appear, apply a cloth made of rose oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; and bind the cloth gently on top until those apostemes are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the wax cloth, and apply a poultice of mill powder with plenty of egg, then put on bandages, and let the bandage on the fracture be always thicker, and a little wider than the others; and know that it should have six bandages on the arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones or two; and tighten more on the fracture than elsewhere, and always less towards the extremities, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 Et, after healing
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 Et si cil prurits ne volt pas estre apaisiez de l’aigue chaude, si aroses le membre d’aigue froide; et se ne volent pas les prurites passer d’eux, si prenes la mervelle de la pome de terre, et fai ung petiz mucielx de celes merveilles et l’osse al membre qui a cil prurits.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 Et se li os se velt desevrer de lien, si covient que tu adresses la cicatrisacion en tel manere com devant dist.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	 Et se il ne volt pas venir a ceste manere, si mettes le membre en eaue froide, et laisse le membre en l’eaue jusqu’à ceo qu’il soit recomfortes de la norrissement, et puis l’estraint.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things happens to the patient, then do not unbind him for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 And if it is in the neck, then let him place his hands on his neck, and let his collarbones be equal, and he should avoid movement and jerking, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty or thirty-five days, and by chance in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	 On the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Know that on the back of the hand and at the base of the fingers, there are few breaks, and only many dislocations occur.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And when the palm of the hand is broken or dislocated, it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged, and sit upright in front of him equally; then place his hand on the outstretched table, and let the assistant straighten the broken bones, and let the physician set them straight until they are well joined; and apply the poultice and wadding, if abscesses do not occur, then place a bandage according to the size of the location; and let it be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 And if the break is around the heel of the foot, make a sphere of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it onto his broken heel; and then secure it with a long strip of cloth, and let the knot be as large as the palm of the hand, and tie it, as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	 And if the break is in the finger, you must place a bandage on top and another underneath the foot, so that the hand remains open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and secure the knot between the toes.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And if the break is in one of the toes, whether it be in the big toe, set it straight as needed; and secure it with the foot, and if you wish, place a small straight bandage to elevate the break, ensuring it does not move; and if the break is in other toes, such as in the thumb or one of the others, set it straight and bind it with the healthy toe next to it; either bind all together in one turn, whichever works best, or place a bandage on top, as for the big toe; and take care in the restoration and disposition of an abscess, and support those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	 Of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it is well seen when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is that one binds a ligament above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And the patient lies on his face, then each attendant extends his ligament to its equal part; and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one of the ligaments should be towards the knee, and the other ligament below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And so if it is near the knee, then let one of the ligaments be by the knee, and let the extension be downwards; then let the surgeon place the bone equally with his two hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice, and bind it, unless a pustule should come there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 Et s’il y a un abcès chaud, alors laisse-le se calmer avant de revenir à ton travail et à ton traitement; le pansement est fait de cette manière.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 It is necessary that you wrap on the break a bandage doubled in two or three layers, leaving the ends hanging; then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the nail, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and let the ends of the thread come up above; then wrap the bandage around the leg and thigh, then place on the break splints, and put one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to even out the tightness, then begin to tie strongly three or four times on the break; and as you go higher on the break, tighten less; then seize the two ends of the thread that you have put between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, until you come near the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, because no abscess or swelling or other similar thing will occur.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And if it happens, dislocate it and address what comes of it, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, one must remove them, if possible; and if not possible, then one must split the place, and draw out strongly; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that one places splints in it, as in the shoulder and in the arm; however, in this restoration the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	 And know that the thigh is restored within five days, or a little less or more, depending on the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	 of the tendon of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the knee joint there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a hole, and this happens in any wound, and without wound, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the restoration is such that one puts equal parts around what is broken to its two sides, so that they are assembled together as much as possible; then apply the poultice, and if necessary, place a round bandage on it, and bind it as needed, then follow all the procedures that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as for abscesses or similar things; then for each accident, apply what is appropriate until it heals.  ?>
de la brisure de la jambe	 of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called by its proper name "tibia", and the other is called "fibula"; and all fractures occur as they do in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is equally so, and the work is entirely the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it well; and it turns downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply traction, and align it well, and bind the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly and there are several fragments, let the traction be lesser and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;
de la brisure des os dou piet	 de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, and aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust,
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	 At the ankle, there is no fracture, but in the foot bones there is sometimes a fracture and in both sides, and it happens more often than dislocation in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 And if there is a fracture in the foot bones, and you see these bones overlapping each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wants to go, and now put your foot on top of his, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their place; then apply a poultice and wool on top, and place a small board with two flat feet underneath the sole of the foot, then bind it evenly around the foot, after which you wrap bandages and other necessary things.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	 And when three days or four have passed, then untie the bandage, for you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 And if there are any of the two bones broken, then set them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint on the broken bone according to its length, and it should be a bit wider; then place under the foot the board that I mentioned earlier, and bind it tightly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, then place a splint on each bone according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and let it rest on top of the board outside the belly of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, just as we have said; and treat each incident as appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	 of the bone of the elbow
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, have her sit with legs spread apart, then lean her back towards the posterior part, and let it be held from behind; then fill the woman's natural cavity with cotton, and put in as much as I (the author) do; then raise the woman up, lifting the buttocks little by little, until the cotton jumps up to the entrance of the nature, and the bone returns with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, put it back, and do this for 7 days or thereabouts: the fracture will be healed, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and attach a reed to its opening, and inflate the entire bladder inside the nature; then blow strongly into the reed, so that the bladder is fully inflated within: the nature will also return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it thus for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bones of the man's fist are broken, or those of the woman, then restore them as we have said in the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from those who apply their study and practice to it, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For the fracture signifies in many dispositions the right way of restoration: pay attention then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose’s throat and put the penis into it; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it there for three days, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	 of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for someone who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, like the thigh bone or shoulder blade or similar, to be cauterized now, so that the cauteries we have mentioned testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 Et si la plaie est saine, retiens-la avec du vitriol, si tu n'as pas autre chose. Puis recommence à restaurer la fracture en cette même heure, ou ce jour-là, si des abcès ne se forment pas là.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if such abscesses come, then leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause harmful accidents to occur.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone appears protruding from under the skin, it is necessary that you delicately bring it back into place with your hands, with a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And if the extension is not suitable for you to bring it back into place with your hands, then use this instrument of iron, which has VII or VIII inches in length, and its width according to the size of the wound; and therefore it is necessary for the physician to have III or IV of these, as needed for each fracture cure; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and let it be pointed at the end, and thicker towards the middle, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche," for which the curved head must be placed on top of the visible bone; and push once, until it returns, and let them be equal one to the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone so that the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 And if you cannot return the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, either a knife or saw, to your ability; then raise that which remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 If it is so that he is in his place, then moisten the bandage in black stiptic wine, and properly if it is in summer; and do not put on the wound cerote or any other thing that has oil, for it will bring putrefaction and corruption; then administer splints when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; and many times have foolish physicians done this, and brought upon the patient either death or putrefaction at certain times; and let the constriction be gentler and softer than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that evil will occur as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then you should not apply bandages; but instead, wrap around hard cloths in place of bandages, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one day or two the swelling increase in the wound, remove all that you have put on the wound, and apply a healing ointment to the wound, such as the ointment tetrapharmacon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	 And it is necessary that you unbind the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and cured.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And it is necessary that the limb be positioned in such a way that the swelling drains downward gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 And if many days pass, and he cannot heal but returns always bowed, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must seek the wound with a tent, and remove all these loose pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, then you must cure it, according to what is said in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the thigh or shoulder bones, and other similar large limbs, do not extract it, for many times death results, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out after 20 or 30 days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 of the blows that come upon the shoulder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 We often see this after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a terrible thing to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Therefore take care if the wound is fresh: and administer astringent medicines such as aloes, frankincense, myrrh, sarcolle, acacia, and similar others; and choose one of these or all together, and make them into a decoction with stiptic wine or with plenty of egg yolk or with mustard; and place them on the knot in lint, and bind it well, and do not untie for many days; and then unbind, and start another, until the nodule is gone; or you can apply it to a piece of lead, well prepared; because the property of lead is such that it removes all swellings on the limbs; and if the nodule has already turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then scrape it off, and make the superfluity apparent; or you can give it to a surgeon, until it is removed, and treat it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	 Of the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 When the fracture of the bone is healed, and afterwards the limb remains weak and thin, this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings and nourishment could not reach the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to excessive movement, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, and so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 And the treatment is such that you make the patient eat and make his body soft, so that the blood may increase in him; and administer baths, and give him joy and merriment; then apply pitch to the limb, so that the pitch attracts great nourishment to it, and frequently wash it with warm water, until the nourishment reaches the limb; and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	 When a limb is twisted after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is open, and the form of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: therefore do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb anew; and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and these actions are blamed, and great evils come from them, and perhaps death; however, if the nodes and tortures are fresh, it is necessary that they be anointed with hot water, or softening herbs be boiled, such as leaves of comfrey, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as well-made diachylon, and take the muslin of comfrey, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or take ripe figs, and grind them with colon powder, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is removed by continually and for a long time rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And let there be gentle movement to the limb each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And if the twist has worsened and hardened, like stone, and needs to be removed with an iron, it must be cut down to the bone with a fine incision; and apply caution and skill in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 A dislocation is a joint moving out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb becomes misshapen, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When a dislocation occurs to someone, it must be immediately reset without delaying.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Car if one delays, then the place swells, and perhaps it is only with difficulty that one can reset it to its place; therefore, it is not appropriate that one moves it when it is swollen: many times this brings on spasm and other pains; however, when this happens, let the patient be bled, then leave him until the abscess has subsided; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then reset it lightly, and treat each member as it comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	 And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	 of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 It often happens that the jaw is dislocated downwards, and the dislocation of both occurs in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their place and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, and saliva runs from the mouth so that it cannot be held back, nor can one close the mouth, and the tongue is wrapped up with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself in many ways.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is whole and complete, then you must quickly reset it, without delaying; and in such a way that the assistant holds the patient's head, and the practitioner puts his finger into one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is from two parts; and let the other two hands be free to balance; and instruct the patient to relax his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the practitioner should keep it balanced until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 And if returning is difficult, even if it is the two jaws together, then apply hot water and oil until you can easily reset them; do not delay in returning them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are brought back into place, and the patient's mouth is closed without softening, a bandage of moistened cloth in cerate made from rose oil and wax is applied, then it is lightly tied with soft ligatures; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head resting between two cushions, so that they do not move to the right or left, nor should they try to chew, but rather take light food until the pain subsides, and the jaws are firmly fastened; then let them gently masticate whatever they wish, and do not struggle to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well fastened and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two mandibles cannot be reset precisely in one hour, and are not returned to their places, then fevers and accustomed sweats result, and perhaps an upset stomach, and perhaps pure bile is vomited.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 And when you see this, then know that it is fatal; and many times the one to whom it happens dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	 of the hammer
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The hammer cannot dislocate from the hip joint, and is sometimes dislocated at the thigh, which is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on his back and stretches out his arms; then press strongly on the place with your palm, and it will return; then apply a poultice and bandage tightly; and the head that is towards the outside cannot dislocate; if not, and if it sometimes dislocates, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply a poultice and the bandage tightly, and command the patient to rest until healed; and similarly the shoulder joint is restored when it has left its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	 From the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 You should know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one is that it dislocates towards the lower part of the armpit; and the second is towards the chest; and sometimes it dislocates upwards, which happens rarely; and it does not dislocate backwards due to the shoulder, nor inwards due to the nerves. And many times it dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially for those who have little flesh, because for them it goes quickly; for those who have enough flesh, it goes with difficulty and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And it happens to some men that they receive a blow or break, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	 It is therefore necessary that you examine it thoroughly until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And the dislocation is known when it goes down towards the shoulder blade, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find manifest diversity between them; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the shoulder blade on the back the head of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way; and so too, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly on the back; and this manner of dislocation is not difficult to reduce when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	 And the manner is that the servant takes the hand of the patient and raises it up, then places his fingers under the arm, and lifts the joint with force up to its place; and the servant raises the hand and extends it up, then places it underneath; thus it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said in a few days after, then the patient must be bathed in hot water; and the servant should prepare a softening and soothing mixture, such as a decoction of althaea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and apply it; then let the patient lie on his back, and place under the arm a pad of wool cloth, neither too soft nor too hard, then the physician places his heel on the pad, and raises the head of the shoulder skillfully, and pulls the hand of the patient; and another servant holds the head of the patient so that it does not move down; this shoulder will return instantly, and if you see it thus, reset it in this manner: and it is necessary for you to have present a man who is larger than the patient; and let him stand straight beside the patient's side, and push his shoulder under the patient's arm, and raise the arm up so that the patient hangs in the air; and another servant pulls the hand of the patient down towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too light, then have them carry something heavy with them, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And it can also be reset in another way: and this is done by driving a long stick into the ground so that its tip is as round as a piston, neither too thick nor too thin; then place the patient on top of it but with soft cushions underneath, and have the patient stand along the length of the stick; then extend his arm downwards on the other side like this, and the joint will return to its place immediately; and if it does not want to return for all these reasons that we have said, then perform this cure: take a stick two arms in length and four thumbs wide, which has a round tip to enter deeply under the armpit according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 Then take the patient and place him on the crossbeam of the scaffold below, so that the beam does not injure the patient. Then place it under the patient's seat; extend one arm along the beam, tie the shoulder to the beam, and the arm at the head of the hand. Then place the arm on the step of a wide ladder, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the joint will now return into place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	 And when it is back in place, by whatever means, it is necessary that you put under the seat an equal piece of wool, then apply the bandage prepared with mill dust, with incense and egg white, on all the shoulder and around, then securely bind it under the seat, and wrap the ligature over the bandage, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 And it is necessary that he rests, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then rest more after V days or VII, and move it; and if it is immobile and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for any other reason, it is necessary that you apply cautery at three points, as described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after VII days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm above, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The dislocation which is towards the foot and breasts, or behind, it is made by impact and extension of the hands, and another method is administered; and cured until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	 And if after healing comes stiffness to the member, and gradually in movement, then the patient should bathe many times until that stiffness is relieved, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	 of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 Know that the shoulder joint is easily dislocated and easily returns; and if it has dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not returned, for one sees it well and feels it well; and it dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick person with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 Because the joint is dislocated and he cannot bend his arm or touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 And you must reset it before any abscesses come there, because if abscesses came there, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is at the back; this is worse than other dislocations and causes greater pain, and sometimes death occurs.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 And the restoration is such that when it can be reset, you extend his hand with your two hands; and let his arm be spread, and the hands of the patient according to the course around, above and below, and push the joint back together, or at the base of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	 And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand on his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm where it is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and it is good that two men extend the arm, and hold it together, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from one side to the other, after you have wrapped a double-long and wide cloth around it; and when the patient joins the joint to his hand, then anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint strongly, until it returns; and when it is in place, then put on a dry plaster with egg white, and hold it firmly, and bind the arm around the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	 And if the joint is fixed in its place, then unbind the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then reapply the bandage and the ligament, and leave it this way for some days, until it is firmly set; then unbind it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels pain after the joint has been reset and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or place a greasy sheepskin on the joint, leave it there for a day and a night, then remove it and have him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint gently, then place the sheepskin back on, and have him re-enter the bath; and do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see [it is not healing], then place warm, moist cow dung mixed with butter on it, and bind it up; thus it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	 The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is light, more than other joints However, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, lest the place become swollen or a hot abscess form.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the return is thus: you place the injured hand on a table, and the minister extends his hand, and the physician places it equally, so that he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns However, it must be seen if it is well in place; then let the patient place the back of his hand on a table for extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 Et si la dislocation est au dos de la main, que le patient place le dos de sa main sur la table, et que le médecin place sa main sur l'apparence de la jointure.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 Si elle revient à nouveau, c'est bon. Sinon, appliquez des emplâtres calmants sur les abscès et laissez-les ainsi sans recommencer.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 Si le patient ne peut pas supporter cela, et que vous ne pouvez pas le remettre en place après quelques jours, alors la jointure reste tordue ; et cela ne nuit pas au patient tant que sa main est humide et qu'il ne peut pas saisir quelque chose : dans ce cas, sachez que les nerfs ou les artères sont coupés ; il n'y a pas d'autre remède que de pratiquer une cautérisation à cet endroit, et peut-être que cela n'aura aucun effet.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	 And when the hand is in place, then apply the plaster that we have mentioned, then restrain it and leave it for five days, then release it and let it be thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he cannot move it well and there is some stiffness, then moisten it with hot water, and rub it until it is supple.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	 of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated at each part, sometimes at the back of the palm or at the front; then stretch out the finger and push the dislocation towards your thumb until it goes back, then support the head of the finger and bend it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for two days, then on that day make it even again; and tie it as we have said, and untie it daily, and make it move, and retie it at night; and do this often, until it is healed, and do the same if it is dislocated at the front of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is supple; and do the same when it is dislocated on another side.  ?>
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	 of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	 When the spine of the back or the neck is dislocated, and there are many dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the sign of this is that the egestions jump out without will, and he cannot hold it in, and often some member is softened, either the two thighs or the two arms or one, and often the spine moves in four parts; that which moves to the back is called "gilbositez": the cure for this is that you turn if the gilbositez comes from childhood: then there is no cure nor healing of all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And those that come from falling or blows or similar things, the ancients speak of cures in grand words, where there is not always great benefit; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the jaundice that comes to the chest first, there is no sense or health; and also that which comes directly on both sides, and one cannot cure except that which properly comes to the back, as I say; and let the patient be stretched out on his back in an equal place, and have support beneath him so he does not injure himself; then drive a stake into the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a ligament under the bed of the patient, and another at the hips, and the knees, and the ankles; and two assistants know how to tighten the ligaments, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and let them be well secured, the stake as we have said, and the healer places his palms on the spine firmly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return with this treatment, take a board three arms long, and place it beneath the surface, and have the patient lie on his side, and push the head of the board beneath the surface, then place the middle of the board upon the spine; and let the physician put his feet upon the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do the same with a tourniquet that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And it is that you insert two stakes at the patient's head one arm's length apart, and towards the feet two others, with half a palm's length between each stake; and let there be in each stake one hole, through which the tourniquet runs, and let the stakes be firmly planted in the ground so that they do not move; and between every two stakes place a turning stake on which the ropes turn, and let there be in the two turning stakes two small stakes of half a palm's length to turn the tourniquet; and then tie the rope that is among the stakes to the tourniquet towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other tourniquet, and each of the assistants turns his tourniquet with all his might, and the master places the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is equalized, then apply a drying plaster with plenty of egg, and then the wool, and then the bandage of a tablet of III fingers in length, which should cover the place of the yellowness and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a string, as we have said, and let the patient use gentle nursing until he is cured; and if something happens at the end of the cure, then you must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the bandage that we have mentioned before; sometimes they administer a piece of lead, and sometimes it appears in the back vertebra of the spine, and one might think it is a dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, which is why one should not be presumptuous: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	 Of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 Know that in the joints of the hip and the shoulder, dislocation only occurs, not as in other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and it is more dislocated on one side than the other, and rarely in front or behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the leg of the patient with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee opens more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend his knee; and the place where the hip comes is swollen with an abscess, because the head of the thigh bone goes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	 And the signs of those to whom it happens due to lack of strength, these accidents are contrary to the previous ones.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.
