And the signs of those to whom it happens in front, is that they hold their leg well according to its length; however, do not bend the knee with pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot move forward, and retains his urine, and the ankle swells, and when walking, passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	 And the signs of those to whom it happens in the rear, is that he cannot extend his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hip is located below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 The treatment of this type of dislocation is such that you must consider whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its condition, then there is no cure; and it should not be presumed.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	 And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, which is one of four types of dislocation, you should hasten to return the joint, and place it inside and out, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you must summon a strong assistant, and place the leg strongly with two hands, or with one hand tied above the knee; and another assistant should extend his hand above in such a way that he pushes his hands under his armpits, then pulls a soft ligament on the thigh; and another holds the end of the rope; and they all pull up and down together at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground in one go, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	 This manner of extension is common to four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If not, it is necessary to apply the remedy accordingly When the dislocation is in the hip, it is necessary that you support the patient on their healthy side, then place the ligament on the root of the thigh, and the place that is under the groin, then extend the ligament upwards towards the groin, and towards the pelvis; then take another assistant his arms, and embrace the large part of the unhealthy thigh, and stretch it strongly: thus it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot clamp it in this manner as we have said, then you must tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong, soft ligature above the two ankles and above the two knees, and the injured leg should be extended two fingers' width more than the other; then let them hang from the top of a pole, and let it be two arm's length off the ground; then command one assistant to embrace the thigh at the hip, and let another assistant hang with the patient, who embraces the thigh strongly, for now the joint returns quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is at an end, let the patient lie down as we have said for those with scoliosis, and tighten the ligature on the injured leg properly, and on the foot likewise; then place two splints, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert a splint between the thighs of the patient in this manner; and let there be placed damp cloths around it, lest the patient be hurt, then let each assistant lean towards him, and the physician should place his hand equal to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place him on the table and press as we have said in the section on dislocation, with the patient lying on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	 And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, according to what I have said; and let the doctor place his foot on the affected ankle, then press with the other hand, extending down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is behind, it is not necessary to extend the affected limb downwards or raise it from the ground, but it should be as if the hip were dislocated behind, as we have said about lying on both hips; and let him lie on his face, with the cord extended as we have said before, and someone should press on the joint against the table; and it will be ready when the patient extends his legs and they are even; then bring the thighs together, and apply a poultice, and bind tightly with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three days or four, then unbind him, and apply another poultice; and if you see that they are even, bind again as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind him, and make him walk well, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	 Of the knee dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	 The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the sign of this is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not approach his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the reduction of all these is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and draw between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee strongly; and another assistant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it approaches his thigh easily; and apply a plaster, and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and bind them together firmly for three days or four, then unbind; and let the patient not work at walking, as long as the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not at all, then administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed
de la dislocation dou talon	 of the ankle's dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	 The ankle is sometimes moved, and sometimes fully dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs are that the ankle is swollen and bent forward at the dislocated part: the reduction is easy, and one should extend it gently with their hands when it is only sprained.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is fully dislocated, then you must make the patient sit upright and have the helpers stand by the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, and then to the left twice, then extend it upwards, and nicely push the foot upwards; and do this two times, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, then begin again, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and drive a firm stake into the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around, so that it does not hurt the patient; then let the helpers take hold of the thigh, and another helper extend the foot in their hands or with one cord, which they tie above the ankle of the foot; then let each helper extend equally, and the stake should always be between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when extending; then the physician should put the dislocation equally in his hands, and another helper take hold of the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, place the dressing and bandages on top, and bind it very tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and protect the nerves that are above the ankle in the back, so that the binding is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the binding softens, bind again; then unbind at the third or fourth day, and prevent the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before this time, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if there are abscesses present, it is necessary that you heal them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	 of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	 When the shoulders are dislocated, it is necessary to straighten them nicely without difficulty, and this is easy.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	 of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation, and you want to restore it, it often happens that the patient dies; so do not be presumptuous in the cure if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and cautious, but bold; and at the beginning use soothing remedies for the hot abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place before the hot abscess comes there; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing remedies for the hot abscess, and treat the wound as necessary with dried onions; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are broken apart, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into a way of fear, according to what I have said, for this avails you according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your arms and body.
Amen	 So be it
